Distinguishing Natural from Educational in Geometrical Entities
Author defines point, line, surface, body as accidents and distinguishes natural from educational.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which geometrical entities are substances (jawhar) and which are accidents (ʿaraḍ) according to the philosophers, and explain why the point is considered simple.

Core Idea
Natural entities are substances; geometrical counterparts are accidents that subsist as boundaries.

This passage from the Sharh al-Tadhhib defines the fundamental geometrical entities—point, line, surface, and body—according to the philosophers (hukama). It introduces a crucial distinction between the natural (ṭabīʿī) entity as a substance composed of matter and form, and the educational (taʿlīmī) entity as an accident inhering in the natural one. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping how the philosophers conceptualize the physical and mathematical worlds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four geometrical entities
The passage defines point, line, surface, and body. Note that each has both a natural and an educational counterpart. The definitions are given in terms of limits: point is the end of a line, line is the end of a surface, surface is the end of a body.
This is a definition by limit (hadd bi al-nihaya), not by genus and differentia.
2
Distinguish natural from educational
Natural line, surface, and body are substances (jawhar) composed of matter and form, and they exist by themselves. Educational line, surface, and body are accidents (ʿaraḍ) that inhere in the natural ones and are their boundaries.
Natural entities are physical; educational are geometrical abstractions.
3
Analyze the definitions by limit
Each educational entity is defined as the end of the next higher entity: point = end of line, line = end of surface, surface = end of body. This chain shows how geometrical concepts are grounded in physical bodies.
The point is the simplest, being the end of a one-dimensional line.
4
Understand the simplicity of the point
The point is an accident that is not divisible in any direction. It is simple (basīṭa) because it lacks extension. In contrast, the line divides in one direction, the surface in two, and the body in three.
This divisibility property distinguishes educational entities from natural ones.
5
Connect to the rejection of atomism
The philosophers reject indivisible atoms (jawhar fard). Natural bodies are continuous and composed of matter and form, not atoms. The point is not an atom but a boundary of a continuous line.
This rejection differentiates the philosophers from the mutakallimun who affirm atomism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في مبادئ التصورات الذي هو نهاية السطح، والسطح ينقسم إلى جهتين: الطول والعرض. والخط ينقسم إلى جهة واحدة هي الطول، والنقطة لا تنقسم إلى جهة ما. واعْلَمْ أَنَّ النَّقطة في اصطلاح الحكماء عبارة عن نهاية الخط. حاصلُهُ أنَّ الحكماء يقولون : إنَّ ما قبل القسمة طولاً ؛ يُقالُ لهُ : خطّ طبيعي، وهو مُركَّب من الهيولى والصُّورة؛ لَا مِنَ الجواهر الفردة ؛ لاستحالة وجودِهَا عندَهُم ، والامتداد القائم بذلك الخط الطَّبيعي القابل للقسمة في جهةِ الطُّولِ؛ يُقال له : خطّ تعليمي، ونهايته النقطة، فكلُّ مِنَ الخطّ التَّعليمي، والنقطة عندَهُم : عَرَض . وإذا وُضِعَ خط طبيعي بجانبِ آخَرَ ؛ بحيثُ صارًا قابلين للقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً ؛ كان الحاصل منهما : سطح طبيعي، والامتداد القائم به القابل للقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً ؛ يُقالُ لَهُ : سطح تعليمي، ونهايته : خط تعليمي . وإذا وُضِعَ سطح طبيعي فوقَ آخَر ؛ كان الحاصل جسماً طبيعيًّا، والامتداد القائمُ بِهِ القابلُ لِلقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً وعمقاً يُقالُ لَهُ : جسم تعليمي، ونهايتُهُ السَّطح، فتحصَّلَ مِن قولِنَا : إنَّ الخطوط والشطوحَ والأجسامَ الطَّبيعيَّة جواهر قائمةٌ بِنَفْسِهَا، مُركَّبَةٌ مِنَ الهيولى والصُّورة عندَهُم ، وأنَّ النُّقطة والخطوط والشطوحَ التَّعليميَّةَ أعراض عندَهُم؛ لا قيامَ لَهَا بِنَفْسِهَا ؛ لأنَّها نهايات وأطراف للمقادير الامتدادات القائمة بالجسم الطَّبيعي؛ أعني : الخطّ، والسطح، والجسم. إذا عَلِمْتَ هذا؛ فقولُ الشَّارحِ : نهاية الخطّ؛ أي: التعليمي، وقوله: (الَّذِي نهاية السطح)؛ أي: التَّعليميّ؛ أي: الذي هو نهاية الجسم التعليمي، فهو عرض يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً وعُمقاً، فهو سطح فوق سطح. والشطحُ التَّعليمي : عرض يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً فقط، والخط التعليمي : عَرَضُ يقبلُ القسمة طولاً فقط، والنُّقطةُ عَرَضُ لا يقبل القسمة أصلاً. (قَوْلُهُ: وَالخَطُّ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى جِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ ... إلخ) أي: فلا يمكن رؤيته؛ لأنَّهُ جوهران؛ لصق أحدهما بجانبِ الآخَر ؛ فينقسم طولاً بجوهرين، لا عرضاً؛ إذْ عرضُهُ جوهر فرد. وأمَّا السَّطْحُ ؛ فهو خطَّانِ وُضِعَ أحدهما بجانب الآخر، فينقسم طولاً إلى خطَّين، وعَرْضاً إلى خطَّين. وأمَّا الجسم؛ فهو سطح فوق سطح، فينقسم طولاً إلى شقين؛ كلُّ شقّ خطّ فوقَهُ خطّ ، وعَرْضاً إلى ذلك أيضاً، وعمقاً إلى سطحين، فتحصل أنَّ النُّقطة بسيطة.
Section: On the principles of concepts. That which is the end of the surface, and the surface divides into two directions: length and width. The line divides into one direction which is length, and the point does not divide into any direction. And know that the point in the terminology of the philosophers is an expression for the end of the line. Its summary is that the philosophers say: That which is before division in length is called a natural line, and it is composed of matter and form, not of indivisible atoms, due to the impossibility of their existence according to them. And the extension subsisting in that natural line, capable of division in the direction of length, is called an educational line, and its end is the point. So both the educational line and the point are, according to them, accidents. And if a natural line is placed next to another such that both become divisible in length and width, what results from them is a natural surface, and the extension subsisting in it, divisible in length and width, is called an educational surface, and its end is an educational line. And if a natural surface is placed above another, what results is a natural body, and the extension subsisting in it, divisible in length, width, and depth, is called an educational body, and its end is the surface. So it is established from our statement that natural lines, surfaces, and bodies are substances subsisting by themselves, composed of matter and form according to them, and that the point, educational lines, and educational surfaces are accidents according to them, having no subsistence by themselves because they are ends and extremities of the quantities, the extensions subsisting in the natural body, namely the line, surface, and body. If you know this, then the commentator's statement: 'the end of the line' means the educational line, and his statement: 'that which is the end of the surface' means the educational surface, meaning that which is the end of the educational body; it is an accident divisible in length, width, and depth, so it is a surface above a surface. The educational surface is an accident divisible in length and width only, the educational line is an accident divisible in length only, and the point is an accident not divisible at all. (His statement: 'And the line divides into one direction... etc.') means: thus it cannot be seen, because it is two substances, one attached to the side of the other; so it divides in length into two substances, not in width, since its width is a single substance. As for the surface, it is two lines placed one next to the other, so it divides in length into two lines, and in width into two lines. As for the body, it is a surface above a surface, so it divides in length into two parts, each part a line above a line, and similarly in width, and in depth into two surfaces. Thus it is established that the point is simple.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the fundamental geometrical concepts—point, line, surface, and body—as understood by the philosophers (hukama). The author begins with a section heading 'On the principles of concepts' and immediately states that the point is the end of the line, the line is the end of the surface, and the surface is the end of the body. These are definitions by limit (hadd bi al-nihaya), not by genus and differentia. The core of the passage distinguishes between natural and educational (or 'ta'limi', i.e., geometrical) entities. Natural lines, surfaces, and bodies are substances (jawhar) composed of matter and form (hayula and sura), and crucially, they are not composed of indivisible atoms (jawhar fard), which the philosophers deny. The educational entities are accidents ('arad) that subsist in these natural substances. For example, the educational line is the extension (imtidad) divisible in length that inheres in the natural line. The point is defined as the end of the educational line, and similarly, the educational surface ends in an educational line, and the educational body ends in an educational surface. The author then explains that these geometrical accidents have no independent subsistence; they are merely boundaries and extremities of the quantities inherent in natural bodies. The commentator further clarifies that the statement 'the line divides into one direction' implies that the line, being two points (or substances) attached, is not visible and divides only in length, not in width. Similarly, the surface divides in both length and width, and the body in three dimensions. The conclusion is that the point is simple (basiṭa) because it has no division.

Key Takeaway
In this philosophical framework, geometrical entities are accidents (boundaries) inhering in natural substances, and the point is simple because it lacks all division.

Definitions of Point, Line, Surface, and Body in Islamic Logic
Defining the four teaching quantities and their divisibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four teaching quantities (point, line, surface, body) based on their accidents and divisibility.

Core Idea
The point does not divide; the line divides in one direction; the surface in two; the body in three.

This lesson introduces the fundamental conceptual quantities (al-maqadir al-ta'limiyya) used in the Islamic rational sciences. These are not physical substances but accidents that serve as the limits of natural bodies. Understanding their definitions and how they divide is essential for grasping the subject matter of geometry, astronomy, and logic.

Guided Path
1
Recognize that these quantities are accidents
Al-Dasooqi emphasizes they are not self-subsistent but are limits of magnitudes in natural bodies.
Accidents (a'rad) subsist in substances; here they are conceptual limits.
2
Note the number of directions of division for each
Body: three (length, width, depth); surface: two (length and width); line: one (length); point: none.
Division is imaginary, not physical.
3
Understand the composition of these quantities
A line is two points side by side; a surface is two lines side by side; a body is two surfaces stacked. Hence the point is simple (basita).
This explains why the point has no division.
4
Distinguish between imaginary and actual division
Al-Atar clarifies that division here is imaginary (takhayyuli) – positing separate parts in the mind – not actual (fi'li) which would produce new entities.
Actual division of a line yields lines, not points.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات
الَّذي هو نهاية السطح، والسَّطح ينقسم إلى جهتين : الطُّولُ والعَرْضُ . والخط ينقسم إلى جهةٍ واحدةٍ هي الطُّول، والنقطة لا تنقسم إلى جهة ما .
الدسوقي: هي الَّتى هو التَّعليميَّةَ ؛ أعراض عندَهُم؛ لا قيامَ لَهَا بِنَفْسِهَا ؛ لأنَّها نهايات وأطراف للمقادير الامتدادات القائمة بالجسم الطَّبيعي؛ أعني : الخطّ، والسطح، والجسم. إذا عَلِمْتَ هذا؛ فقولُ الشَّارحِ : نهاية الخطّط؛ أي: التعليمي، وقوله: (الَّذِي نهاية السطح)؛ أي: التَّعليميّ؛ أي: الذي هو نهاية الجسم التعليمي، فهو عرض يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً وعُمقاً، فهو سطح فوق سطح. والشطحُ التَّعليمي : عرض يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً فقط، والخط التعليمي : عَرَضُ يقبلُ القسمة طولاً فقط، والنُّقطةُ عَرَضُ لا يقبل القسمة أصلاً. (قَوْلُهُ: وَالْخَطُّ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى جِهَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ ... إلخ) أي: فلا يمكن رؤيته؛ لأنَّهُ جوهران لصق أحدهما بجانبِ الآخَر ؛ فينقسم طولاً بجوهرين، لا عرضاً؛ إذ عرضُهُ جوهر فرد . وأمَّا السَّطْحُ ؛ فهو خطَّانِ وُضِعَ أحدهما بجانب الآخر، فينقسم طولاً إلى خطَّين، وعَرْضاً إلى خطَّين. وأمَّا الجسم؛ فهو سطح فوق سطح، فينقسم طولاً إلى شقين؛ كلُّ شقّ خطّ فوقَهُ خطّ ، وعَرْضاً إلى ذلك أيضاً، وعمقاً إلى سطحين، فتحصل أنَّ النُّقطة بسيطة.
العطار: (قَوْلُهُ: وَالخَطُّ يَنْقَسِمُ تُطلقُ القسمة على معنيين؛ الوهمية: وهي فرضُ شيءٍ غير شيء، والفعلية : وهي إحداث هويَّتين في المقسوم؛ والَّذِي مِن خواص الكم الَّذي المقدار قسم منه هو الأولى، وأمَّا الثَّانيةُ؛ فَلَا يَقبلُها كما بينَ في محله .
Section on the principles of conceptualizations. That which is the end of the surface, and the surface divides into two directions: length and width. The line divides into one direction which is length, and the point does not divide into any direction. al-Dasooqi: They are the ones which are the teaching [quantities]; accidents according to them; they have no subsistence by themselves because they are ends and extremities of the magnitudes which are extensions subsisting in the natural body; namely: line, surface, and body. When you know this, the commentator's saying: 'the end of the line' i.e. the teaching line, and his saying: 'that which is the end of the surface' i.e. the teaching surface; i.e. that which is the end of the teaching body. So it is an accident that accepts division in length, width, and depth, so it is a surface on top of a surface. The teaching surface: an accident that accepts division in length and width only. The teaching line: an accident that accepts division in length only. The point: an accident that does not accept division at all. (His saying: 'The line divides into one direction...' etc.) i.e. it cannot be seen; because it is two essences (jawharān) placed side by side; so it divides lengthwise into two essences, not widthwise; since its width is a single essence (jawhar fard). As for the surface, it is two lines placed side by side, so it divides lengthwise into two lines, and widthwise into two lines. As for the body, it is a surface on top of a surface, so it divides lengthwise into two parts; each part is a line above a line, and widthwise likewise, and depthwise into two surfaces. Hence it results that the point is simple. al-Atar: (His saying: 'The line divides...') The word 'division' is used in two senses: imaginary division, which is positing something as not something, and actual division, which is bringing about two identities in the divided. That which is among the properties of continuous quantity, which is magnitude, is the first sense; the second is not accepted by it as explained in its place.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is a section on the principles of conceptualizations (mabadi' al-tasawwurat). It defines the fundamental geometric quantities: point, line, surface, and body. The main commentator (Dasooqi) explains that these are accidents (a'rad) because they are limits (nihayat) of magnitudes which subsist in natural bodies. The teaching quantities (jism ta'limi, sath ta'limi, khatt ta'limi, nuqtah) are conceptual entities used in mathematics. The author then details how each accepts division: the teaching body divides in three dimensions (length, width, depth); the surface in two (length and width); the line in one (length only); and the point not at all. An interesting note: the line is said to be composed of two 'essences' (jawharayn) placed side by side, which is a reference to the view that the line is made of two points. The surface is two lines side by side, and the body is two surfaces stacked. The point is simple (basitah). Al-Atar adds a clarification about the term 'division' (qismah), distinguishing between imaginary division (takhayyuli, conceptual) and actual division (fi'li, physical). The division of quantities is conceptual, not actual, because if you actually cut a line you do not get points but smaller lines. This precision guards against misunderstanding the nature of these divisions. In the Islamic intellectual tradition, these distinctions are important for defining the subject matter of the rational sciences, especially in logic and natural philosophy.

Key Terms

الخط
السطح
الجسم التعليمي
القسمة

B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
The four teaching quantities are accidents distinguished by the number of dimensions in which they accept imaginary division: point (0), line (1), surface (2), body (3).

?

Geometrical Quantities as Accidents and the Point's Non-Quantity
Defines point, line, surface as accidents and critiques an error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key properties of mathematical quantities (body, surface, line, point) and explain why the point is not a quantity based on the criterion of divisibility.

Core Idea
Geometrical quantities are accidents; the point is not a quantity because it lacks divisibility.

This passage from the Tadhheeb al-Mantiq explores the nature of geometrical quantities: point, line, surface, and the mathematical body. It establishes that these are all accidents subsisting in natural bodies and clarifies the composition of lines from points, surfaces from lines, and bodies from surfaces. More importantly, it corrects a common error: thinking that the point is a quantity (kamm), because quantity is defined by its ability to accept division—which the point does not. The passage also refines our understanding of the commentator's claim about the mathematical body. Through this lesson, you will learn to apply the definition of quantity to test whether something qualifies as a magnitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entities and their status
Read the opening sentence: 'والكل أعراض غير مستقلة الوجود'. What are 'all' referring to? It includes point, line, and surface. They are said to be accidents (a'rad) not independent in existence. What does that mean? They do not subsist by themselves but inhere in substances.
The phrase 'غير مستقلة الوجود' means they are not self-subsisting; they depend on a substance.
2
Understand the composition claim
Al-Dasuqi explains that a line is composed of two points, a surface of four points, and a body of eight points. This shows how geometrical entities are built from points. But note: the point itself is not divisible—it is the building block.
This composition is not physical but conceptual in the mathematical sense.
3
Define quantity (al-kamm)
The passage defines quantity as 'continuous quantity that is stable in essence and divisible into mathematical body and surface'. The key property: divisibility (qabūliyyat al-qisma). Anything that is divisible along its dimensions is a quantity. The point has no dimensions and thus cannot be divided.
Compare with the definition of magnitude: it must be divisible.
4
Analyze the critique of the point as quantity
The author says that considering the point as part of magnitude is a 'gross error' (khaṭaʾ fāḥish). Why? Because the point does not accept division, while magnitude is defined by having parts. Check: Does the point have length, width, or depth? No. So it fails the condition of quantity.
The pronoun 'الكل' in the phrase 'والكل أعراض' was misinterpreted to include the point as a magnitude; the author corrects this.
5
Resolve the confusion about the mathematical body
The commentator (al-Muḥāshī) claimed that the author made the mathematical body an end of magnitude, which is wrong. The author clarifies that the mathematical body is itself a magnitude, not an end. The ends are line and surface. This distinction prevents confusing the abstract mathematical body with the natural body.
The mathematical body (al-jism al-ta'līmī) is the subject of geometry, subsisting in the natural body.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكلُّ أعراض غير مستقلَّةِ الوجودِ ؛ لأنَّها نهايات وأطراف للمقادير على ما بُيِّنَ في كتب الحِكمَةِ . الدسوقي والخطَّ مُركَّب من نقطتين، والشطح من أربع نقط، والجسم من ثمان نقط، هذا توضيح كلام الشارح . (قَوْلُهُ : غَيْرُ مُسْتَقِلَّةِ الْوُجُوْدِ) أي: لا تقومُ بِنَفْسِهَا ، أو إنَّما تقوم بالجوهر . وقولُهُ: (لأنّها نهايات)؛ أي: لأنَّ مجموعها نهايات، وإلا ؛ فالجسم التعليمي ليس نهايةَ الشَّيء، تأمل. (قَوْلُهُ: وَأَطْرَافٌ لِلْمَقَادِيْرِ) أي: الخط والشطح، والجسم التعليمية، وهي الامتدادات القائمة بالجواهر، وهي الخطُ الطَّبيعي، والشطحُ الطَّبيعي، والجسم العطار والخطّ وهو (قَوْلُهُ : وَالْكُلُّ) أي : النُّقطة والخطُّ والسّطح، لكنَّ الخطّ والشطحَ بِاتِّفاق؛ لأنهما مِنَ المقدارِ المعرَّف بأنَّهُ الكَمُ المُتَّصِلُ القارُّ الذَّات المنقسم إلى الجسم التعليمي والسطح، وأمَّا النُّقطةُ ؛ فسيأتي الكلام فيها ، والمثبت للمقدار هو الحكماء، والمتكلمونَ نَفوهُ، ثمَّ إِنَّ الجسمَ التَّعليمي ينتهي بالسطح، وهو بالخطّ بالنُّقطة سُمِّيَ جسماً تعليميا ؛ لأنَّهُ مَوضوعُ العُلومِ التَّعليميَّةِ ؛ كالسطح والخطّ التَّعليميَّيْنِ ، وهذا الجسم التعليمي هو الكَمِّيَّةُ القائمة بالجسمِ الطَّبيعي، وهو الجسم المتحيّز الشارية فيه، ويُسمى باعتبارِ كَونِهِ حَشواً مَا بينَ السَّطوح : ثخناً، وباعتبار كونه نازلاً من فوق : عُمقاً، وباعتبارِ كَونِهِ صَاعداً من تحت سمكاً، وقولُ المحشي : والكُلُّ : أعراض؛ أي: للجسمِ التَّعليميّ، وكذلِكَ قوله بعدَ أنْ نقل عبارةَ شرحِ الطَّوالعِ : وَبِهِ تعلمُ مَا في كلامِ الشَّارح بالنسبة للجسمِ التّعليمي؛ حيثُ جعله نهاية لِلمقدارِ ؛ عدول عن الصَّوابِ، أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلَمَّا بَيَّنَّا أَنَّها قائمة بالجسم الطَّبيعي، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَليسَ كلامِ الشَّارح ذِكْرُ الجسمِ التّعليميّ، بَلْ إِنَّما ذكرَ الخطَّ والسّطح . (قَوْلُهُ : لِأَنَّهَا نِهَايَاتٌ) قال البعضُ : الصَّميرُ - وهو اسم ـ إِنْ وقعَ على النُّقطة والخط والشطح والمقدارِ الَّذي هُوَ كَم؛ أقسامُهُ تلكَ الثَّلاثةُ مَعَ الجسمِ التَّعليمي .ا.هـ. وهذا خطأ فاحش ، فإنَّهُ لا يقولُ عاقل فَضْلاً عَنْ فاضل؛ بأنَّ النُّقطةَ مِنْ مَقولة في
And all are accidents not independent in existence because they are ends and extremities of magnitudes as explained in books of wisdom. Al-Dasuqi: The line is composed of two points, the surface of four points, and the body of eight points; this is clarification of the commentator's speech. His saying: 'not independent in existence' means they do not subsist by themselves, or rather they subsist by substance. And his saying: 'because they are ends' means because their totality is ends; otherwise the mathematical body is not the end of a thing, reflect. His saying: 'and extremities of magnitudes' means the line, surface, and mathematical body, and they are extensions subsisting in substances, which are the natural line, natural surface, and natural body. Al-Attar: And the line... He said: 'And all' means the point, line, and surface, but the line and surface by agreement because they are of magnitude defined as continuous quantity, stable in essence, divisible into mathematical body and surface. As for the point, discussion will come later. The affirmers of magnitude are the philosophers, and the theologians negated it. Then the mathematical body ends with the surface, and it ends with the line and the point; it is called mathematical body because it is the subject of the mathematical sciences, like the mathematical surface and line. This mathematical body is the quantity subsisting in the natural body, which is the body occupying space and being in it. It is called, considering it as filling between surfaces: thickness, considering it descending from above: depth, and considering it ascending from below: thickness. The commentator's saying: 'and all are accidents' means for the mathematical body, and likewise his saying after quoting the expression of Sharh al-Tawali': 'and by it you know what is in the commentator's speech regarding the mathematical body, where he made it an end of magnitude, a deviation from correctness. As for the first, because we have shown that they subsist in the natural body; as for the second, the commentator's speech does not mention the mathematical body, but rather he mentioned the line and surface.' His saying: 'because they are ends' – some said: the pronoun – which is a noun – if it refers to the point, line, surface, and magnitude which is quantity, its divisions are those three with the mathematical body. This is a gross error, for no sane person, let alone a learned one, says that the point is of the category of quantity, let alone being part of magnitude which is one of its divisions. For the point does not accept division, and quantity has the property of accepting division.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the nature of geometrical quantities. It begins by stating that all such entities (point, line, surface) are accidents, not independent substances, because they are the ends and extremities of magnitudes. The commentator then clarifies that a line is composed of points, a surface of lines, and a body of surfaces, elaborating on the definition of magnitude (al-kamm al-muttasil). The author critiques a mistaken view that the point is part of magnitude, arguing that a point does not accept division, which is a necessary property of quantity. The passage also distinguishes the mathematical body (al-jism al-ta'limi) from the natural body, noting that the former is the subject of mathematical sciences and subsists in the latter. The commentary includes a correction of the original commentator's statement, pointing out that he did not claim the mathematical body is an end of magnitude but only the line and surface. This refines the understanding by preventing confusion between the mathematical and natural.

Key Terms
الكم
الجسم التعليمي
النقطة
الخط
السطح
العرض

Checkpoint
Why is a point not considered a quantity (kamm) according to this passage?
A) Because it has no length, width, or depth.
B) Because it does not accept division.
C) Because it is a substance.
D) Because it is not an accident.

Key Takeaway
The point is not a quantity because it lacks divisibility, a necessary property of magnitude; it is merely an accident and an end of a line.

?

?

Defining Body: Theologians' View and Mu'tazilite Nuances
Presents the theologians' definition of body and the Mu'tazilite view on intermediate entities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the theologians' definition of body, distinguish the Mu'tazilite definition, and explain the role of essential line and surface as intermediate substances.

Core Idea
Theologians define body as divisible magnitude; Mu'tazilites add essential line and surface between atom and body.

What exactly is a 'body' in Islamic theology? This passage from al-Dasuqi's commentary on al-Tadhib clarifies the theologians' definition and contrasts it with the philosophers'. It also unpacks the Mu'tazilite view that recognizes essential lines and surfaces as intermediate substances between the indivisible atom and the body.

Guided Path
1
Locate the core definition of body
Find the sentence: 'الجسم هو المتحيز القابل للقسمة'. This is the general theologians' definition. Note that 'divisible' can be even in one dimension.
This is from Ahl al-Sunna.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite definition
The text says: 'وقالت المعتزلة: هو الطويل العريض العميق'. They require three dimensions. They also define line (one dimension) and surface (two dimensions) as separate substances.
3
Understand the hierarchy of magnitude
Magnitude (المقدار) is divisible quantity. It divides into line (length only), surface (length and width), and body (length, width, depth).
This is a logical division used in kalam.
4
Distinguish schools on intermediate entities
For Mu'tazilites, line and surface are essential substances (جوهرية) between atom and body. For Ahl al-Sunna, they are included within the definition of body and are not separate substances.
This difference affects debates on composition of bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات وعند المتكلمين : الدسوقي الطَّبيعيُّ ؛ لأنَّ المقدارَ عندهم هو الكمُ القابل للقسمة، وهو إما خط؛ إنْ قبلها طولاً، وسطح ؛ إن قبلها طولاً وعَرْضاً وجسم؛ إن قبلها طولاً وعرضاً وعمقاً، وعطفُ (الأطرافِ) على (النّهاياتِ) تفسير (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ هذا مُقابل لكلام الحكماء، والمراد بالمتكلمين؛ ما يشمل أهل السُّنَّةِ والمعتزلة . المطار الكم، فضلاً عن كونها من المقدارِ الَّذي هو أحد أقسامِهِ، فَإِنَّ النُّقطة لا تقبلُ القِسمةَ ، والكَمُ مِنْ خواصه قبول القسمة. (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ المُتَكَلِّمِينَ ... إِلَخ) اِعلَمْ أنَّ الجسم هو المتحيّز القابل للقسمة؛ وَلَو في جهةٍ واحدةٍ، وقالَتِ المعتزلةُ : هُوَ الطَّويلُ العريض العميقُ ، فَالمركَّبُ مِن جزأين أو ثلاثة؛ ليسَ جوهراً فرداً ولا جسماً عندَهُم ، فَالمنقَسِمُ في جهةٍ واحدةٍ يُسمُونَهُ خَطَّا، وفي جِهَتَيْنِ : سَطحاً، وهُمَا واسطتَانِ بين الجوهر الفرد والجسمِ عندهم، ودَاخِلَانِ في الجسم عندَنَا ، فثبتَ أنَّ بعض المتكلمينَ - وَهُمْ فرقةٌ مِنَ المعتزلة - يَقولونَ بالخطّ الجوهري والشطح الجوهري، وقد صرَّحَ بِذلِكَ ملا زاده في شرح الهداية، وأمَّا النُّقطةُ ؛ فَلَا يقولُ بِهَا المتكلمونَ؛ لأنَّهم نَافُونَ لِلمقدارِ الَّتي هِيَ طرفٌ لِأَحَدٍ أقسامِهِ، وهو الخط ، وأثبتوا الجوهر الفرد، إذا علمت هذا؛ فَقَوْلُ الشَّارحِ : ويتألفُ الجسمُ مِنَ السُّطوحِ ... إلخ؛ مُوَافِقٌ لهذا المذهب، ويرد عليه مُؤاخذتان؛ الأُولَى : إيهامُ كلامِهِ أنَّ هذا مِمَّا اتَّفق عليه المتكلمونَ؛ حيث قابل مذهبهم بالحكماء، وليس كذلك، وقد يتعذَّرُ بأنَّهُ ليسَ بِصددِ تَقريرِ مَذاهب القوم؛ بَلْ ذكر استطراداً فيكفي الإجمال، الثَّانيةُ قَولُهُ: والخُطوطُ مِنَ النُّقَطِ صَرِيحٌ فِي أَنَّ المتكلّمِينَ يَقولونَ بالنُّقطة، وليس كذلِكَ، وأيضاً الكلامُ هُنَا في الخط والشطح الجوهريَّين، والنُّقطةُ عَرْضُ، فَلَا يتألفُ مِنها الجوهر، لا يُقالُ : أرادَ بِهَا الجوهر الفرد ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يُسمِّيهِ مُثبتوهُ بِذَلِكَ كَمَا نُصَّ عليهِ في الكتب الكلاميَّةِ، وَمَا في
Chapter: On the principles of concepts. And according to the theologians: Al-Dasuqi: The natural [body] because magnitude according to them is quantity divisible; it is either line if it accepts length only, surface if it accepts length and width, and body if it accepts length, width, and depth. And the conjunction of 'extremities' to 'ends' is an explanation. His saying: 'And according to the theologians' – this is a counterpart to the speech of the philosophers, and by theologians is meant what includes the Sunnis and Mu'tazilites. Al-Mutar: Quantity, let alone being part of magnitude which is one of its divisions; for the point does not accept division, and quantity has the property of accepting division. His saying: 'And according to the theologians... etc.' Know that the body is that which occupies space and is divisible, even in one dimension. The Mu'tazilites said: It is the long, wide, deep; so what is composed of two or three parts is neither an indivisible atom nor a body according to them. So what is divisible in one dimension they call a line, in two dimensions a surface; these are intermediaries between the indivisible atom and the body according to them, and are included in the body according to us. So it is established that some theologians – a group of the Mu'tazilites – affirm the essential line and essential surface. Mulla Zadeh explicitly stated this in his commentary on al-Hidaya. As for the point, the theologians do not affirm it because they negate magnitude which is an extremity of one of its divisions, namely the line, and they affirm the indivisible atom. If you know this, then the commentator's saying: 'And the body is composed of surfaces... etc.' agrees with this school. Two objections are raised against him: first, his speech implies that this is agreed upon by all theologians, since he contrasted their school with the philosophers, but it is not so. It is excusable by saying that he is not in the position of reporting the schools of the people, but mentioned it incidentally, so generality suffices. Second, his saying: 'And the lines are from points' clearly indicates that the theologians affirm the point, but it is not so. Also, the discussion here is about the essential line and surface, and the point is an accident, so substance is not composed of it. It cannot be said that he meant by it the indivisible atom, because we say: its affirmers do not call it by that name, as stated in theological books. And what is in...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a definitional chapter on the principles of concepts (mabadi' al-tasawwurat) focusing on the theologians' definition of body. It begins by contrasting the philosophers' view with that of the theologians (mutakallimun), who define magnitude as divisible quantity. The text explains that according to the theologians, a body is that which occupies space and is divisible, while the Mu'tazilites specifically define it as long, wide, deep. The passage clarifies that the Mu'tazilites consider a line (one dimension) and a surface (two dimensions) as intermediate entities between the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) and the body; these are essential (johari) for them. The commentator then critiques a misunderstanding: the original sharh (commentary) claimed that theologians hold that lines are composed of points, which would imply they affirm the point. However, the theologians generally deny the point because it is not a magnitude and they affirm the indivisible atom instead. Two objections are raised against the sharh: (1) it misleadingly suggests unanimity among theologians, and (2) it incorrectly ascribes the point to them. The passage refines the understanding by distinguishing the views of different groups, particularly the Mu'tazilites, and correcting the misattribution.

الجسم
الجوهر الفرد
الخط الجوهري
السطح الجوهري
المقدار
الكم

C) Mu'tazilites deny the existence of line and surface, while Ahl al-Sunna affirm them.

Key Takeaway

Correcting Misattributions: The Commentator's Error on Points and Surfaces
Critiques the commentator's misattribution of points to theologians and clarifies the non-unanimous nature of the surfaces view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two objections al-Dasuqi raises against the commentator's claim that theologians affirm points and lines composed of points.

Core Idea
Al-Dasuqi corrects the commentator: theologians deny points, and the view that body is composed of surfaces is not unanimous.

Commentators sometimes err in attributing views to entire schools. In this passage, al-Dasuqi critiques the commentator (likely al-Taftazani) for two mistakes: first, implying that the view that body is composed of surfaces is agreed upon by all theologians, and second, claiming that theologians say lines are from points. This lesson dissects these objections and clarifies the actual theological position on points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two objections against the commentator
The text says: 'فَقَوْلُ الشَّارحِ ... إلخ؛ مُوَافِقٌ لهذا المذهب، ويرد عليه مؤاخذتان'. Find the two objections: first, the commentator's wording implies unanimity; second, his phrasing 'الخطوط من النقط' imputes belief in points to theologians.
2
Analyze the first objection: implied unanimity
The commentator's statement 'ويتألف الجسم من السطوح' (the body is composed of surfaces) is attributed to the theologians in general, but only some Mu'tazilites hold that. Ahl al-Sunna do not.
Al-Dasuqi excuses it as incidental mention but still notes the error.
3
Analyze the second objection: points
The commentator said 'والخطوط من النقط' (lines are from points). But theologians deny points because they affirm the indivisible atom and consider points as accidents, not substances.
The passage explicitly states: 'وأما النقطة فلا يقول بها المتكلمون' (As for the point, the theologians do not affirm it).
4
Confirm the correct view on points
The point is an accident (عرض), not a substance (جوهر), so a body cannot be composed of points. Even if 'point' meant the indivisible atom, its affirmers do not call it a point.
This clarifies the terminology.

Source Text

فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات وعند المتكلمين : الدسوقي الطَّبيعيُّ ؛ لأنَّ المقدارَ عندهم هو الكمُ القابل للقسمة، وهو إما خط؛ إنْ قبلها طولاً، وسطح ؛ إن قبلها طولاً وعَرْضاً وجسم؛ إن قبلها طولاً وعرضاً وعمقاً، وعطفُ (الأطرافِ) على (النّهاياتِ) تفسير (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ الْمُتَكَلِّمِينَ هذا مُقابل لكلام الحكماء، والمراد بالمتكلمين؛ ما يشمل أهل السُّنَّةِ والمعتزلة . المطار الكم، فضلاً عن كونها من المقدارِ الَّذي هو أحد أقسامِهِ، فَإِنَّ النُّقطة لا تقبلُ القِسمةَ ، والكَمُ مِنْ خواصه قبول القسمة. (قَوْلُهُ : وَعِنْدَ المُتَكَلِّمِينَ ... إِلَخ) اِعلَمْ أنَّ الجسم هو المتحيّز القابل للقسمة؛ وَلَو في جهةٍ واحدةٍ، وقالَتِ المعتزلةُ : هُوَ الطَّويلُ العريض العميقُ ، فَالمركَّبُ مِن جزأين أو ثلاثة؛ ليسَ جوهراً فرداً ولا جسماً عندَهُم ، فَالمنقَسِمُ في جهةٍ واحدةٍ يُسمُونَهُ خَطَّا، وفي جِهَتَيْنِ : سَطحاً، وهُمَا واسطتَانِ بين الجوهر الفرد والجسمِ عندهم، ودَاخِلَانِ في الجسم عندَنَا ، فثبتَ أنَّ بعض المتكلمينَ - وَهُمْ فرقةٌ مِنَ المعتزلة - يَقولونَ بالخطّ الجوهري والشطح الجوهري، وقد صرَّحَ بِذلِكَ ملا زاده في شرح الهداية، وأمَّا النُّقطةُ ؛ فَلَا يقولُ بِهَا المتكلمونَ؛ لأنَّهم نَافُونَ لِلمقدارِ الَّتي هِيَ طرفٌ لِأَحَدٍ أقسامِهِ، وهو الخط ، وأثبتوا الجوهر الفرد، إذا علمت هذا؛ فَقَوْلُ الشَّارحِ : ويتألفُ الجسمُ مِنَ السُّطوحِ ... إلخ؛ مُوَافِقٌ لهذا المذهب، ويرد عليه مُؤاخذتان؛ الأُولَى : إيهامُ كلامِهِ أنَّ هذا مِمَّا اتَّفق عليه المتكلمونَ؛ حيث قابل مذهبهم بالحكماء، وليس كذلك، وقد يتعذَّرُ بأنَّهُ ليسَ بِصددِ تَقريرِ مَذاهب القوم؛ بَلْ ذكر استطراداً فيكفي الإجمال، الثَّانيةُ قَولُهُ: والخُطوطُ مِنَ النُّقَطِ صَرِيحٌ فِي أَنَّ المتكلّمِينَ يَقولونَ بالنُّقطة، وليس كذلِكَ، وأيضاً الكلامُ هُنَا في الخط والشطح الجوهريَّين، والنُّقطةُ عَرْضُ، فَلَا يتألفُ مِنها الجوهر، لا يُقالُ : أرادَ بِهَا الجوهر الفرد ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : لا يُسمِّيهِ مُثبتوهُ بِذَلِكَ كَمَا نُصَّ عليهِ في الكتب الكلاميَّةِ، وَمَا في
Chapter: On the principles of concepts. And according to the theologians: Al-Dasuqi: The natural [body] because magnitude according to them is quantity divisible; it is either line if it accepts length only, surface if it accepts length and width, and body if it accepts length, width, and depth. And the conjunction of 'extremities' to 'ends' is an explanation. His saying: 'And according to the theologians' – this is a counterpart to the speech of the philosophers, and by theologians is meant what includes the Sunnis and Mu'tazilites. Al-Mutar: Quantity, let alone being part of magnitude which is one of its divisions; for the point does not accept division, and quantity has the property of accepting division. His saying: 'And according to the theologians... etc.' Know that the body is that which occupies space and is divisible, even in one dimension. The Mu'tazilites said: It is the long, wide, deep; so what is composed of two or three parts is neither an indivisible atom nor a body according to them. So what is divisible in one dimension they call a line, in two dimensions a surface; these are intermediaries between the indivisible atom and the body according to them, and are included in the body according to us. So it is established that some theologians – a group of the Mu'tazilites – affirm the essential line and essential surface. Mulla Zadeh explicitly stated this in his commentary on al-Hidaya. As for the point, the theologians do not affirm it because they negate magnitude which is an extremity of one of its divisions, namely the line, and they affirm the indivisible atom. If you know this, then the commentator's saying: 'And the body is composed of surfaces... etc.' agrees with this school. Two objections are raised against him: first, his speech implies that this is agreed upon by all theologians, since he contrasted their school with the philosophers, but it is not so. It is excusable by saying that he is not in the position of reporting the schools of the people, but mentioned it incidentally, so generality suffices. Second, his saying: 'And the lines are from points' clearly indicates that the theologians affirm the point, but it is not so. Also, the discussion here is about the essential line and surface, and the point is an accident, so substance is not composed of it. It cannot be said that he meant by it the indivisible atom, because we say: its affirmers do not call it by that name, as stated in theological books. And what is in...
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a definitional chapter on the principles of concepts (mabadi' al-tasawwurat) focusing on the theologians' definition of body. It begins by contrasting the philosophers' view with that of the theologians (mutakallimun), who define magnitude as divisible quantity. The text explains that according to the theologians, a body is that which occupies space and is divisible, while the Mu'tazilites specifically define it as long, wide, deep. The passage clarifies that the Mu'tazilites consider a line (one dimension) and a surface (two dimensions) as intermediate entities between the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) and the body; these are essential (johari) for them. The commentator then critiques a misunderstanding: the original sharh (commentary) claimed that theologians hold that lines are composed of points, which would imply they affirm the point. However, the theologians generally deny the point because it is not a magnitude and they affirm the indivisible atom instead. Two objections are raised against the sharh: (1) it misleadingly suggests unanimity among theologians, and (2) it incorrectly ascribes the point to them. The passage refines the understanding by distinguishing the views of different groups, particularly the Mu'tazilites, and correcting the misattribution.

Checkpoint
According to al-Dasuqi, why is the commentator's statement 'lines are from points' incorrect?
A) Theologians affirm points, but the commentator used the wrong term.
B) Theologians deny points because they are accidents, not substances.
C) The commentator meant atoms, but the text is about lines.
D) The commentator was correct; al-Dasuqi misunderstood.

Key Takeaway
Al-Dasuqi's critique highlights the importance of precise attribution in commentary: not all theologians agree on composition from surfaces, and points are not part of kalam physics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a statement in a kalam commentary that attributes a view to 'the theologians' generally. Is it really unanimous? Check a primary source like al-Ash'ari's Maqalat to see if there is disagreement.
?
Construct a two-objection analysis of a statement from a fiqh or usul commentary that seems to attribute a view too broadly. Use al-Dasuqi's method: first objection for implied unanimity, second for specific factual error.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
10 min
Definitions of Body, Line, Surface, and Point in Kalam
Defines jism, sath, khatt according to mutakallimin and critiques the commentator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the theologians' definitions of body, line, surface, and point from the philosophers', and identify the two objections raised against the commentator in this passage.

Core Idea
Theologians define body as a composite of indivisible atoms, not as a continuous mathematical extension.

In this passage, the commentator Dusuqi explains the principles of concepts according to the theologians (mutakallimin), contrasting their views with those of the philosophers. You will learn the precise definitions of body, line, surface, and point within the kalam tradition, and see how the commentator's errors reveal the importance of accuracy in reporting doctrinal positions. The passage also introduces the key atomistic framework that underlies much of Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions of body
Find how the theologians (including Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila) define body. The passage gives two definitions: for the theologians in general, body is 'the locus (mutahayyiz) receptive to division, even in one dimension'; for the Mu'tazila specifically, it is 'the long, wide, deep'.
The Mu'tazili definition is more specific and excludes composites of two or three atoms from being a body.
2
Understand substantial line and surface
The passage explains that some Mu'tazila affirm a substantial line (khatt jawhari) composed of two indivisible atoms side by side, divisible in length. A substantial surface (sath jawhari) is composed of two such lines side by side. These are separate substances, not mathematical abstractions.
The philosophers' mathematical line and surface are denied; they are considered mental considerations with no real existence.
3
Analyze the status of the point
The point (nuqta) is the endpoint of a line. Philosophers consider it real, but theologians deny its substance. Some Mu'tazila equate the point with the indivisible atom (jawhar fard), but generally, theologians do not affirm the point as a separate entity.
This distinction is crucial for the critique of the commentator.
4
Extract the two objections against the commentator
First, the commentator's statement implies that the substantial line and surface are agreed upon by all theologians, but they are only affirmed by some Mu'tazila. Second, he says lines are composed of points, which would mean theologians affirm the point, but they do not; the point is an accident, not a substance, and the discussion is about substantial lines.
The commentator's errors stem from conflating different theological positions and from using imprecise terminology.

وهي النُّقطة عندَهم - أمرٌ اعتباري أيضاً لا وجودَ له، فإذا وُضِعَ خطّ مؤلَّفٌ مِن جوهريْنِ فردَيْنِ بجانبِ آخَرَ كذلك؛ كَانَ الحاصلُ مِن مجموع الخطَّيْنِ ؛ سطحاً يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً، والامتداد القائم ـه الذي يُسمّيه الحكماء سطحاً تعليميا ، يُنكرون وجوده، ويقولون : إنَّه أمر به اعتباري، وإذا وُضِعَ سطح مُركَّبٌ مِن أربع جواهر فردة فوق سطح آخَرَ مثله؛ كانَ الحاصل من مجموع الشطحين؛ جسماً يقبل القسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً وعُمقاً، والامتداد القائمُ بِهِ الَّذي يُسمّيه الحكماء جسماً تعليميا ؛ يُنكرون وجوده، ويقولونَ: إِنَّهُ أَمرُ اعتباري، فتحصَّلَ أنَّ هذهِ الثَّلاثةَ ، وَهِي الخط والسطح، والجسم؛ جواهر مُستقلَّةُ الوجودِ، وهذا كلام المعتزلة وبعض أهلِ السُّنَّةِ . وقال بعضُ أهل السُّنَّةِ : ما تركَّبَ مِنْ جوهرين فأكثر ؛ فهو جسمٌ، وَلَا يقولونَ بالخطّ وَلَا بالسَّطْحِ الجوهري، فضلاً عن التعليمي. (قَوْلُهُ : أَشْيَاءُ مُسْتَقِلَهُ الْوُجُوْدِ) لأَنَّهَا نَفْسُ الجواهر . قَوْلُهُ : السُّطُوحِ) «أل» جنسيَّةُ تُبطل معنى الجمعية؛ لأنَّ الجسم يتألف من سطحين فأكثر . (قَوْلُهُ : فِي الْعُمْقِ) أي : في جهةِ العمقِ ؛ بحيثُ يكون سطح فوقَ آخَر . Chapter: On the Principles of Concepts. And according to the theologians: [Dusuqi:] The natural; because magnitude for them is quantity receptive to division, and it is either a line if it receives division in length, a surface if it receives division in length and width, and a body if it receives division in length, width, and depth. And the conjuncting of 'extremities' to 'endpoints' is an interpretation. (His statement: 'And according to the theologians') This is in contrast to the discourse of the philosophers, and by 'theologians' is meant what includes Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila. [Al-'Attar?] Quantity, let alone being part of magnitude which is one of its divisions, for the point does not accept division, and quantity is characterized by acceptance of division. (His statement: 'And according to the theologians... etc.') Know that the body is the locus (mutahayyiz) receptive to division, even in one dimension. The Mu'tazila said: It is the long, wide, deep. So what is composed of two or three parts is neither an indivisible atom nor a body for them. So what divides in one dimension they call a line, and in two dimensions a surface, and these two are intermediates between the indivisible atom and the body for them, and they are included in the body for us. So it is established that some theologians—a group from the Mu'tazila—affirm the substantial line and substantial surface. Mulla Zadeh has stated this in his commentary on al-Hidayah. As for the point, the theologians do not affirm it because they deny magnitude which is an endpoint for one of its divisions, namely the line, and they affirm the indivisible atom. If you know this, then the commentator's statement: 'And the body is composed of surfaces... etc.' is consistent with this doctrine. Two objections are raised against it: The first: his words imply that this is agreed upon by the theologians, since he contrasted their doctrine with that of the philosophers, but it is not so. It may be excused by saying that he is not in the position of reporting the sects' doctrines, but rather mentioned it incidentally, so a summary suffices. The second: his statement: 'And lines are from points' is explicit that the theologians affirm the point, but it is not so. Also, the discussion here concerns the substantial line and surface, and the point is an accident, so a substance is not composed of it. It cannot be said that he meant by it the indivisible atom, because we say: its affirmers do not call it by that, as is stated in the theological books. What is in the logical [works] is that these three are independent existents. And the body is composed of surfaces that are composed in depth, and the surfaces from lines. [Dusuqi:] The summary of what they said: The line is what is composed of two indivisible atoms such that it accepts division in length. As for the extension inhering in it that the philosophers call a mathematical line, they say it is a mental consideration with no existence. And the endpoint of the line—which is the point for them—is also a mental consideration with no existence. So if a line composed of two indivisible atoms is placed next to another such line, the result of the sum of the two lines is a surface that accepts division in length and width. The extension inhering in it that the philosophers call a mathematical surface, they deny its existence and say it is mental. And if a surface composed of four indivisible atoms is placed above another such surface, the result of the sum of the two surfaces is a body that accepts division in length, width, and depth. The extension inhering in it that the philosophers call a mathematical body, they deny its existence and say it is mental. So it is established that these three—line, surface, and body—are independent substances. This is the statement of the Mu'tazila and some Ahl al-Sunna. And some Ahl al-Sunna said: What is composed of two or more atoms is a body, and they do not affirm the substantial line or surface, let alone the mathematical. (His statement: 'independent existents') because they are the very substances. (His statement: 'surfaces') 'Al' is generic, negating the meaning of plurality, because the body is composed of two or more surfaces. (His statement: 'in depth') i.e., in the dimension of depth, such that a surface is above another. (His statement: 'from lines') 'Al' is generic, because the surface is composed of two or more lines. 'Al' [al-'Attar's] gloss: From [the fact] that the point and the indivisible part are one, so it is easy [?] as his statement: The definition of length as the longer of two extensions, width as the shorter, and depth as that which intersects them is refuted by square bodies. End quote. Its correct form is 'by the cube body, which has its three dimensions equal.'
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and critical commentary on the principles of concepts (mabadi' al-tasawwurat) according to the theologians (mutakallimin). It begins by contrasting the philosophical view of magnitude (al-miqdar) as continuous quantity with the theologians' view. The commentator Dusuqi explains that for the theologians, magnitude is quantity receptive to division, and it is divided into line (length), surface (length and width), and body (length, width, depth). Then he discusses the term 'theologians' as including both Ahl al-Sunna and Mu'tazila. The core of the passage revolves around the definitions of body, surface, and line, and the existence of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). The Mu'tazila define body as 'the long, wide, deep' and deny that what is composed of two or three parts is a body or an atom. They call what divides in one dimension a 'line' and in two dimensions a 'surface', considering these as intermediates between the atom and the body, while Ahl al-Sunna include them in the body. Some Mu'tazila affirm a substantial line and surface (khatt jawhari, sath jawhari), but deny the mathematical line and surface of the philosophers. The commentator Dusuqi then critiques the earlier commentator (likely al-Akhdari or another) for implying that theologians universally affirm the point (nuqta) and that lines are composed of points. He raises two objections: first, that the statement suggests consensus when there is none; second, that it erroneously attributes affirmation of the point to theologians, whereas they deny it because they reject mathematical points and instead affirm the indivisible atom. He points out that the discussion concerns substantial line and surface, and the point is an accident, not a substance, so it cannot constitute a line. The passage then explains the Mu'tazili construction: a line is two atoms side by side, a surface is two such lines side by side, and a body is two such surfaces stacked. These are all independent substances (jawahir mustaqillat al-wujud). Finally, a gloss by al-'Attar corrects a definition of length, width, and depth, stating that the refutation by square bodies should be by cube bodies where all dimensions are equal. This passage is crucial for understanding the metaphysical commitments of the theologians in contrast to the philosophers, particularly regarding the nature of space and extension.

Key Terms
جسم
خط
سطح
نقطة
جوهر فرد

C) An independent substance composed of atoms

Key Takeaway
The theologians define body as a composite of indivisible atoms, and the commentator's errors highlight the need for precision when reporting doctrinal differences.

Three Schools on the Nature of the Point
Three schools on the classification of the point (nuqta)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three schools on the point (nuqta) and explain how each affects the validity of using the point as an example for a simple species.

Core Idea
The point's logical classification varies: it is either a simple species, a concept, or a quality - and this determines how definitions work.

In this passage, al-'Attar presents three schools (madhahib) concerning the nature of the point (nuqta). The point is used as an example for a simple species in logic. Understanding these schools is crucial because they affect whether the point can be a proper example for definitions and how genus and differentia apply to simples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three schools
List the three views: (1) it is a simple existent species not under a category; (2) it is a conceptual thing; (3) it falls under the genus of quality.
2
Examine the grounds for each school
The first school relies on the point as a real simple substance; the second treats it as mental; the third classifies it as a quality specific to quantities.
3
Determine the impact on the example
The validity of using the point as an example for a simple species depends on which school you adopt.
4
Relate to the broader discussion
This leads to the question of mental vs external composition and whether simples can have definitions.

(قَوْلُهُ: ثُمَّ التَّمْثِيلُ بِالنُّقْطَةِ) أي : للنَّوعِ الحقيقي، وقوله: (إذا كانَتِ النُّقطة)؛ أي: مفهومها، وهو نهاية الخطّ ، أو الجوهر الَّذي لا يقبل القسمة على الخلافِ بين المتكلمين والحكماء. العطّار (قَوْلُهُ : ثُمَّ التَّمْثِيلُ بِالنُّقْطَةِ ... إلخ) فيها مَذاهب ثلاثة : الأَوَّلُ : أَنَّها نَوعٌ مَوجودٌ بسيط لم يندرج تحت مقولة، وَصِحَةُ التَّمثيل مبنيَّةٌ عليهِ؛ لَا عَلَى أَنَّهَا مِنَ الأمورِ الاعتباريَّةِ كَمَا في الحاشية، فإنَّهُ سَهْو الثَّاني : أنَّها أمر اعتباريُّ الثَّالثُ أَنَّها داخلةٌ تحتَ جنسِ الكَيْفِ، وحصرُ الكيف في أقسامِهِ الأربعةِ، وَهِيَ الكيفيات النَّفسانيَّةُ والكَيفيَّاتُ المحسوسة وكَيفيَّاتُ الكَمِّيَّاتِ والكيفيات الاستعداديَّة ؛ استقرائي، فَهِيَ واردةٌ على الحصر، على أنَّ مير زاهد نقل أَنَّ الشَّيخَ صرَّحَ في التَّعليقاتِ بِأَنَّ النُّقطةَ كَيفيَّةٌ في الخطّ كَالتَّربيع .ا.هـ. فتكون داخلةٌ تحت قشم الكيفيات المختصة بالكميَّاتِ، ثمَّ قضيَّةُ تعريف النقطة بأنَّها شيءٌ ذو وضع ... إلخ؛ أنْ يكونَ مَفهومُهَا مُركَّباً، وَهُوَ كَذَلِكَ كَمَا تقدَّمَ ، والبسيطُ إِنَّما هو ماصدقها، قالَ زاهد: وقد اختُلِفَ في التركيب الذهني والخارجي على ثلاثة أقوال ؛ الأَوَّلُ : أَنَّهما لا يجتمعان أصلاً، والثاني : أنَّهما قد يجتمعان والثَّالثُ : أَنَّهما مُتَلازِمَانِ، ومَا يقتضيهِ النَّظرُ الصَّائِبُ والفِكْرُ الثَّاقِبُ ؛ هُوَ القولُ الثَّالِثُ ؛ لأنَّ مِصداق حَمْل الجنسِ والفَصْلِ ومنشأ انتزاعهما ليس إلا نفس الموضوع ، ونحن نعلم بالضرورةِ أنَّ الحيثية الواحدة لا تكونُ منشأ الانتزاع للمفهومات المتعدّدة ومصداقاً لِحَمْلِهَا، فَيلزمُ أَنْ يكونَ في نفس الموضوع تكثرُ ، وَمَا وقعَ مِنْ تَحديدِ البسائط وإطلاق الجنس والفصل لَهَا ؛ فَمِنْ قَبيلِ المسامحة، قالَ الشَّيخُ في التَّعليقات : الحدُّ لَهُ أجزاء، والمحدود قد لا يكونُ لَهُ أجزاء، وذَلِكَ إذا كان بسيطاً، وحينئذٍ يخترعُ العقلُ شَيئاً يقوم مقام الجنس، وشيئاً يقومُ مَقامَ الفصل، وأمَّا في المركَّب؛ فإِنَّ الجنسَ يُناسِبُ المادَّةَ، والفصل يُنَاسِبُ الصُّورةَ ، وقَالَ الفارابي في تعليقاتِهِ : البسائِطُ لا فصلَ لَهَا ؛ فَلَا فصل لِلونٍ وَلَا لِغيرِهِ مِنَ البسائط، وإنَّما الفصلُ للمركَّبات، وإِنَّما يُحاذى بالفصل الصُّورةُ؛ كَمَا يُحاذَى بالجنس المادَّة .ا.هـ. وإن أردتَ استيفاء الكلام في هذا المقام ؛ فَارجِعْ لِحَواشينا التي كتبناها على المقولات.
Chapter: On the principles of conceptions. [Things] composed in width, and lines from points composed in length; thus they are not accidents, but substances. Then the example by the point is only valid if the point is complete. Al-Dasuqi: His words: 'in width' i.e., in the direction of width; such that one line is beside another line. What the commentator mentioned is a method, and there is a method of the theologians, which is that the body is composed of two or more substances. Al-Akwa?: His words: 'from the points' is generic, so it applies to two or more, and the preferable is from individual atoms; because the point according to them is a conceptual thing, so a self-subsistent existent is not composed from it; unless it is said that it is leniency, so the individual atom, which is the indivisible part, is called a point, even if it is not called that by the verifiers. His words: 'Then the example by the point' i.e., for the true species. And his words: 'if the point is' i.e., its concept, which is the end of the line, or the substance that is not divisible, according to the disagreement between theologians and philosophers. Al-'Attar: His words: 'Then the example by the point... etc.' There are three schools concerning it: First: that it is a simple existent species not falling under a category, and the validity of the example is based on it, not on it being a conceptual thing as in the gloss, for that is an oversight. Second: that it is a conceptual thing. Third: that it falls under the genus of quality. And the enumeration of quality into its four divisions — which are psychic qualities, sensible qualities, qualities of quantities, and dispositional qualities — is inductive, so it is an induction upon the enumeration. Moreover, Mir Zahid transmitted that the Shaykh declared in the Ta'liqat that the point is a quality in the line like quadrature. So it falls under the division of qualities specific to quantities. Then the consequence of defining the point as 'a thing having a position... etc.' is that its concept is composite, and it is so as previously mentioned, and the simple is only its referent. Zahid said: And there is disagreement over mental and external composition according to three sayings: First: that they never coexist. Second: that they may coexist. Third: that they are concomitant. What correct consideration and penetrating thought require is the third saying, because the referent of the predication of genus and differentia and the source of their abstraction is nothing but the subject itself, and we know necessarily that one aspect cannot be the source of abstraction for multiple concepts and a referent for their predication, so multiplicity is necessary in the subject itself. And what has occurred of defining simples and applying genus and differentia to them is from leniency. The Shaykh said in the Ta'liqat: The definition has parts, but the defined may have no parts, and that is when it is simple, and then the intellect invents something that stands in place of the genus and something that stands in place of the differentia. As for the composite, the genus corresponds to matter and the differentia corresponds to form. Al-Farabi said in his Ta'liqat: Simples have no differentia; there is no differentia for color nor for other simples. Differentia is only for composites. The differentia corresponds to form, as the genus corresponds to matter. And if you want exhaustive discussion of this topic, refer to our glosses written on the Categories.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) refining the discussion on the nature of the point (nuqta) as used in defining lines and surfaces. The author follows the commentator's division of two methods: one based on compounds of points, and another by the theologians who say body is composed of two atoms. The point is problematic because it can be viewed as a conceptual entity or a real substance. The author then presents three schools (madhahib) on the point: (1) it is a simple species not falling under any category, (2) it is a conceptual thing, (3) it falls under the genus of quality (kayf). The third view is supported by Mir Zahid's transmission from the Shaykh that the point is a quality like quadrature. The author also discusses the definition of the point as 'a thing having a position', which implies a composite concept, though the referent may be simple. This leads to a discussion on mental and external composition (al-tarkib al-dhihni wa al-khariji) with three opinions: they never coexist, they may coexist, or they are concomitant. The author favors the third, arguing that the same subject must have multiple aspects to support different predicates. The passage concludes with citations from the Shaykh and al-Farabi that for simples, definitions are by leniency—the intellect invents a genus and differentia for comprehension.

التصورات
الجنس
الفصل
الكيف
التركيب الذهني والخارجي

Defining Simples: Genus and Differentia by Leniency
The treatment of definitions for simple entities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why simples like the point are defined by leniency (musamaha) and how the intellect invents a genus and differentia for comprehension.

Core Idea
Simples have no real genus or differentia; definitions for them are intellectual constructs, not real.

After discussing the three schools, the author turns to a deeper issue: how can simples (like the point) be defined if they have no parts? The passage explains that for simples, the intellect invents a genus and differentia by leniency, while for composites, the genus corresponds to matter and differentia to form. The discussion includes al-Farabi's denial of a differentia for simples.

Guided Path
1
Understand the problem
If a simple has no parts, how can it have a definition (hadd) which requires parts (genus and differentia)?
2
Examine the solution from the Shaykh
The definition has parts, but the simple may not; the intellect invents a genus and differentia.
3
Compare with composites
In composites, genus corresponds to matter, differentia to form.
4
Consider al-Farabi's stricter view
He says simples like color have no differentia; differentia only for composites.
5
Identify the three opinions on mental and external composition
The author favors the third: they are concomitant, because the same subject must have multiple aspects to support multiple predicates.

Chapter: On the principles of conceptions. [Things] composed in width, and lines from points composed in length; thus they are not accidents, but substances. Then the example by the point is only valid if the point is complete. Al-Dasuqi: His words: 'in width' i.e., in the direction of width; such that one line is beside another line. What the commentator mentioned is a method, and there is a method of the theologians, which is that the body is composed of two or more substances. Al-Akwa?: His words: 'from the points' is generic, so it applies to two or more, and the preferable is from individual atoms; because the point according to them is a conceptual thing, so a self-subsistent existent is not composed from it; unless it is said that it is leniency, so the individual atom, which is the indivisible part, is called a point, even if it is not called that by the verifiers. His words: 'Then the example by the point' i.e., for the true species. And his words: 'if the point is' i.e., its concept, which is the end of the line, or the substance that is not divisible, according to the disagreement between theologians and philosophers. Al-'Attar: His words: 'Then the example by the point... etc.' There are three schools concerning it: First: that it is a simple existent species not falling under a category, and the validity of the example is based on it, not on it being a conceptual thing as in the gloss, for that is an oversight. Second: that it is a conceptual thing. Third: that it falls under the genus of quality. And the enumeration of quality into its four divisions — which are psychic qualities, sensible qualities, qualities of quantities, and dispositional qualities — is inductive, so it is an induction upon the enumeration. Moreover, Mir Zahid transmitted that the Shaykh declared in the Ta'liqat that the point is a quality in the line like quadrature. So it falls under the division of qualities specific to quantities. Then the consequence of defining the point as 'a thing having a position... etc.' is that its concept is composite, and it is so as previously mentioned, and the simple is only its referent. Zahid said: And there is disagreement over mental and external composition according to three sayings: First: that they never coexist. Second: that they may coexist. Third: that they are concomitant. What correct consideration and penetrating thought require is the third saying, because the referent of the predication of genus and differentia and the source of their abstraction is nothing but the subject itself, and we know necessarily that one aspect cannot be the source of abstraction for multiple concepts and a referent for their predication, so multiplicity is necessary in the subject itself. And what has occurred of defining simples and applying genus and differentia to them is from leniency. The Shaykh said in the Ta'liqat: The definition has parts, but the defined may have no parts, and that is when it is simple, and then the intellect invents something that stands in place of the genus and something that stands in place of the differentia. As for the composite, the genus corresponds to matter and the differentia corresponds to form. Al-Farabi said in his Ta'liqat: Simples have no differentia; there is no differentia for color nor for other simples. Differentia is only for composites. The differentia corresponds to form, as the genus corresponds to matter. And if you want exhaustive discussion of this topic, refer to our glosses written on the Categories.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a super-commentary (hashiya) refining the discussion on the nature of the point (nuqta) as used in defining lines and surfaces. The author follows the commentator's division of two methods: one based on compounds of points, and another by the theologians who say body is composed of two atoms. The point is problematic because it can be viewed as a conceptual entity or a real substance. The author then presents three schools (madhahib) on the point: (1) it is a simple species not falling under any category, (2) it is a conceptual thing, (3) it falls under the genus of quality (kayf). The third view is supported by Mir Zahid's transmission from the Shaykh that the point is a quality like quadrature. The author also discusses the definition of the point as 'a thing having a position', which implies a composite concept, though the referent may be simple. This leads to a discussion on mental and external composition (al-tarkib al-dhihni wa al-khariji) with three opinions: they never coexist, they may coexist, or they are concomitant. The author favors the third, arguing that the same subject must have multiple aspects to support different predicates. The passage concludes with citations from the Shaykh and al-Farabi that for simples, definitions are by leniency—the intellect invents a genus and differentia for comprehension.

For simple entities, definitions are lenient intellectual constructs; only composites have real genus and differentia corresponding to matter and form.

Jins al-Ajnas: The Highest Genus in a Chain
Author defines jins al-ajnas and explains ascending arrangement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the highest genus (jins al-ajnas) in an ascending chain of genera and explain why it is so called.

Core Idea
The highest genus has no genus above it and is called 'genus of genera' because of its supreme generality.

In logic, the five universals include genus (jins) and species (naw'). Genera can be arranged in an ascending hierarchy, each genus subsuming lower genera. The apex of such a chain is the highest genus, known as jins al-ajnas. This lesson will help you recognise this concept and understand how it functions in classification, especially in Islamic sciences like fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term 'jins al-ajnas' in the passage
Locate the phrase 'ويسمى ذلك العالي جنس الأجناس' and note its context: it refers to the highest genus in an ascending arrangement.
The text gives 'animal' as an example of jins al-ajnas.
2
Understand the condition for being jins al-ajnas
The passage states that jins al-ajnas has no genus above it. Confirm that it is predicated of all subordinate genera in answer to 'what is it?' (mā huwa).
This is the defining characteristic: it is the end of the upward hierarchy.
3
Contrast with isolated genus (jins mufrad)
The text also mentions that some genera are isolated, having neither a genus above nor below. Note that jins al-ajnas is always at the top of a chain, while jins mufrad does not belong to any chain.
Not every genus is part of a hierarchy; some stand alone.
4
Apply the concept to an Islamic science example
Consider the genus of 'ibadah (worship) in fiqh. Its highest genus might be 'action' (fi'l) if there is no wider genus above. This helps in defining and classifying acts of worship.
This illustrates the practical relevance of jins al-ajnas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في مبادئ التصورات، ثم الأجناس قد تترتب متصاعدة بأن يكون جنس فوقه جنس، وهكذا إلى الجنس العالي. قال الدسوقي: قوله: قد تتربت، «قد» للتحقيق لا التقليل، وأتى بـ«قد»؛ لأن بعض الأجناس لا ترتيب فيه، وهو الجنس المفرد؛ أي: الذي ليس فوقه جنس، وليس تحته جنس، بل تحته أنواع كالعقل المطلق، فإنه جنس مفرد. قال العطار: قوله: ثم الأجناس قد تترتب أشار بلفظ «قد» إلى أن الترتيب في الأجناس مما لا يجب؛ كما لا يجب في الأنواع أيضاً، فكما يكون نوع إضافي لا نوع فوقه ولا تحته؛ فيكون مفرداً غير واقع في سلسلة الترتيب؛ كذلك يكون جنس لا جنس فوقه ولا تحته؛ فيكون مفرداً غير واقع في سلسلة الترتيب. ويسمى ذلك العالي جنس الأجناس كالحيوان مثلاً، فإنه جنس. قال الدسوقي: قوله: ويسمى جنس الأجناس إنما كان العالي من الأجناس يسمى بجنس الأجناس؛ لأن جنسية الشيء باعتبار العموم بعد أن يكون مقولاً في جواب ما هو.
Chapter: On the principles of concepts. Then genera may be arranged ascendingly, such that a genus has a genus above it, and so on until the highest genus. Al-Dasuqi said: His saying 'qad tatarattabu' – 'qad' is for confirmation, not for diminution; he brought 'qad' because some genera have no arrangement in them, namely the isolated genus: i.e., that which has no genus above it and no genus below it, but rather species below it, like absolute intellect, for it is an isolated genus. Al-'Attar said: His saying 'then the genera may be arranged' – by the word 'qad' he indicated that arrangement in genera is not necessary, just as it is not necessary in species either; so just as there is a relative species that has no species above it nor below it, being isolated and not occurring in the chain of arrangement, likewise there is a genus that has no genus above it nor below it, being isolated and not occurring in the chain of arrangement. And that highest one is called 'genus of genera' (jins al-ajnas), like animal for example, for it is a genus. Al-Dasuqi said: His saying 'and it is called genus of genera' – the highest of the genera is only called 'genus of genera' because the genus-ness of a thing is by virtue of generality after being said in answer to 'what is it?'.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage from a commentary on logic (sharh) introduces the concept of genera arranged ascendingly. The author states that genera may be arranged in an ascending order, each genus having a higher genus above it, until reaching the highest genus. The commentators then clarify that the word 'qad' (may) indicates that this arrangement is not necessary—some genera are isolated (jins mufrad), having neither a genus above nor below them, with only species under them. An example is absolute intellect (al-'aql al-mutlaq), which is considered an isolated genus because it has no genus above it. The highest genus in an ascending chain is called 'jins al-ajnas' (genus of genera), such as 'animal' in relation to its subordinate genera. Al-Dasuqi explains that the term 'jins al-ajnas' is used because the genus-ness of a thing is based on its generality and its being predicated in answer to 'what is it?'.

Key Terms
جنس الأجناس
الجنس المفرد
قد

Checkpoint

A) It has no genus above it and is the highest in an ascending chain.
B) It has no species below it.
C) It is predicated of only one species.
D) It is an accident and not a substance.

Key Takeaway
Jins al-ajnas is the terminal genus in an ascending chain, defined by having no genus above it and being predicated of subordinate genera in answer to 'what is it?'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Al-Jins al-Mufrad: The Isolated Genus
Author defines isolated genus (jins mufrad) and explains its place in the theory of genera.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish an isolated genus (jins mufrad) from a hierarchical genus and identify its characteristics.

Core Idea
Not all genera are part of a hierarchy; some are isolated, having no genus above or below them.

In the previous lesson, we saw that genera can ascend to a highest genus. But the commentators point out that this arrangement is not necessary. Some genera stand alone, neither subsumed under a higher genus nor having a genus below them. These are called isolated genera (al-jins al-mufrad). This lesson focuses on identifying and understanding such genera.

Guided Path
1
Find the description of jins mufrad in the passage
Look for the phrase 'الجنس المفرد' and note its definition: it has no genus above it and no genus below it, but only species under it.
The text gives 'absolute intellect' (al-'aql al-mutlaq) as an example.
2
Understand why the term 'qad' is used
The word 'qad' in 'قد تترتب' indicates possibility, not necessity, because isolated genera exist. This warns against assuming all genera are hierarchical.
Al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar both emphasise this point.
3
Contrast with arranged genera
Compare isolated genus with genera that form a chain (like animal as jins al-ajnas). Note the difference: isolated genus has no higher genus, but also no lower genus; it is not part of any ascending or descending sequence.
An isolated genus is not the same as jins al-ajnas, which is the top of a chain.
4
Reflect on the example: absolute intellect
Consider why absolute intellect is considered an isolated genus. It has species (e.g., human intellect, angelic intellect) but no higher genus because it is a simple, non-composite entity that cannot be classified under a broader category.
This example shows that isolation can arise from the nature of the concept.

Source Text
