The Definiens: Predicate That Gives Concept
Author defines the definiens and its relation to the five universals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two essential conditions for a valid definiens and distinguish it from ordinary predication in Islamic definitional contexts.

Core Idea
The definiens is not just any predicate – it must give the concept of the thing.

Now that we have the five universals as raw materials, we need to know how to use them to build definitions. This lesson focuses on the definiens itself: what makes a statement a genuine definition rather than just an informative sentence. The author clarifies that a definiens must be predicated on the thing with the specific aim of conveying its concept (tasawwur). Al-Dasuqi's commentary sharpens this by introducing the key notion of 'predication of agreement' (haml muwata'a) and by excluding statements that merely describe a state.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of al-mu'arraf
In the Arabic, find the sentence that defines al-mu'arraf. It begins with 'مُعَرِّفُ الشَّيْءِ مَا يُقَالُ عَلَيْهِ' meaning 'The definiens of a thing is what is predicated on it.'
This is the core definition you need to remember.
2
Identify the two parts of the definition
The definition has two parts: (1) 'what is predicated' (genus) - a predicate in a sentence; (2) 'for the purpose of giving its concept' (differentia) - the specific aim. Mark these in the translation.
The differentia is crucial: it excludes predications that only give information about a state.
3
Understand haml muwata'a
Al-Dasuqi explains that 'what is predicated' means predication of agreement, where subject and predicate are mutually convertible in meaning. For example, 'Zayd is a human' is haml muwata'a, but 'Zayd is standing' is not because 'standing' is not identical with Zayd.
This ensures the predicate truly expresses the essence of the subject.
4
Apply the condition to an example
Consider the sentence 'Human is a rational animal.' Check if it satisfies both conditions: it predicates 'rational animal' on 'human' (condition 1) and it gives the concept of human (condition 2). It qualifies as a definiens.
Now compare with 'Human is a writer' – it predicates but does not give the full concept.
5
See how the five universals relate
The passage states that the five universals (excluding common accident) are the principles (mabadi') of concepts. This means definitions are constructed from genus, species, differentia, property, and common accident (though common accident is excluded here).
The definiens aims to capture the essence using these universals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَمَبَادِئُ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ الْكُلِّيَّاتُ الْخَمْسُ. وَمَقَاصِدُهَا: الْمُعَرِّفُ، وَالْقَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ. وَالْمُصَنِّفُ لَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنْ مَبَاحِثِ وَمَبَادِئِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ، شَرَعَ فِي الْمَقَاصِدِ، فَقَالَ: [حَدُّ الْمُعَرِّفِ] (مُعَرِّفُ الشَّيْءِ مَا يُقَالُ عَلَيْهِ؛ أَيْ: عَلَى الشَّيْءِ الْإِفَادَةِ تَصَوُّرِهِ).
وَقَالَ الدُّسُوقِيُّ: (قَوْلُهُ: فَمَبَادِئُ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ) أَيْ فَالْمَبَادِئُ الَّتِي تَتَحَصَّلُ مِنْهَا مَقَاصِدُ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ. (قَوْلُهُ: الْكُلِّيَّاتُ الْخَمْسُ) أَيْ مَا عَدَا الْعَرَضَ الْعَامَّ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَأْتِي مِنْهُ تَعْرِيفٌ كَمَا سَيَقُولُ. (قَوْلُهُ: وَمَقَاصِدُهَا) أَيِ الْمَقْصُودُ لِأَجْلِ إِفَادَتِهَا. (قَوْلُهُ: الْمُعَرِّفُ وَالْقَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ) أَيْ لِأَنَّهُمَا يُقْصَدُ لِلتَّوَصُّلِ بِهِ لِلْمُعَرَّفِ، وَالْعَطْفُ لِلتَّفْسِيرِ. (قَوْلُهُ: لَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنْ مَبَاحِثِ وَمَبَادِئِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ) أَيْ لَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنَ الْقَضَايَا الَّتِي يُبْحَثُ فِيهَا عَنْ مَبَادِئِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ، وَهِيَ الْكُلِّيَّاتُ الْخَمْسُ. (قَوْلُهُ: مَا يُقَالُ) أَيْ شَيْءٌ يُحْمَلُ عَلَيْهِ حَمْلَ مُوَاطَأَةٍ؛ بِأَنْ يُجْعَلَ الشَّيْءُ مَوْضُوعاً وَالْمُعَرَّفُ مَحْمُولاً، وَهَذَا شَامِلٌ لِحَمْلِ قَائِمٍ عَلَى زَيْدٍ فِي "زَيْدٌ قَائِمٌ" مَثَلاً، وَلَكِنَّ قَوْلَهُ: (الْإِفَادَةِ ... إِلَخ) يُخْرِجُهُ.
So the principles of concepts are the five universals. And their aims are the definiens and the explicatory statement. When the author finished the investigations and principles of concepts, he began the aims and said: [The definition of the definiens] (The definiens of a thing is what is predicated on it, i.e., on the thing, for the purpose of giving its concept). Al-Dasuqi said: His statement: 'So the principles of concepts' means the principles from which the aims of concepts are derived. His statement: 'the five universals' means excluding the common accident, because no definition comes from it, as he will say. His statement: 'and their aims' means what is intended for the sake of giving them. His statement: 'the definiens and the explicatory statement' means because they are intended to arrive at the thing defined, and the conjunction is for explanation. His statement: 'when he finished the investigations and principles of concepts' means when he finished the propositions in which he discussed the principles of concepts, and they are the five universals. His statement: 'what is predicated' means something that is predicated on it with predication of agreement (haml muwata'a), such that the thing is made the subject and the definiens is the predicate. This includes the predication of 'standing' on Zayd in 'Zayd is standing' for example, but his statement: 'for the purpose of giving its concept' excludes that.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage defines the 'definiens' (المعرف) after establishing that the principles of concepts are the five universals (excluding common accident, as it cannot constitute a definition). The aims of concepts are the definiens and the explicatory statement, which are essentially the same thing (the conjunction is explanatory). The author then gives the definition: 'The definiens of a thing is what is predicated on it for the purpose of giving its concept.' Al-Dasuqi expands on this by explaining that 'what is predicated' means a predicate that is in agreement (haml muwata'a), where the subject and predicate are identical in meaning. For example, 'Zayd is standing' would technically be included, but the phrase 'for the purpose of giving its concept' excludes such cases because the predication in 'Zayd is standing' is not intended to convey the concept of Zayd but rather to inform about his state. The aim of the definiens is specifically to provide a conceptual understanding (tasawwur) of the thing defined.

Key Terms
المعرف
القول الشارح
حمل مواطأة
الكليات الخمس

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the statement 'Zayd is standing' NOT a valid definiens?
A) Because 'Zayd is standing' does not predicate anything on Zayd.
B) Because 'Zayd is standing' is not a predication of agreement (haml muwata'a).
C) Because 'Zayd is standing' does not give the concept of Zayd; it only informs about his state.
D) Because 'Zayd is standing' uses a common accident, which is excluded from definitions.

Key Takeaway
A valid definiens must be a predicate that agrees in meaning with the subject and is specifically aimed at giving the concept of the thing defined.

The Purpose of Predication in Definition
Author defines mu'arif and explains predication is for conception not assent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish predication for conception from predication for assent and apply this distinction to definitions in Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Definitional predication is for conception, not for assent.

This passage defines the term 'mu'arif' (definiens) and clarifies the purpose of predication (haml) within a definition. While predication is commonly used to affirm a property of a subject (tasdiq), in definition it serves a distinct function: to convey the concept (tasawwur) of the definiendum. By examining the commentary of Al-Dasuqi and Al-‘Attar, we will uncover why the primary intention of a definition is conceptual depiction, not assertion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term
Locate the term being defined in the Arabic passage. It is 'المعرف' (al-mu'arif). Note its relationship to 'المعرف بالكسر' (definiens) and 'المعرف بالفتح' (definiendum).
The term mu'arif is the definiens, the predicate in a definition.
2
Extract the definition of mu'arif
Find the precise wording: 'معرف الشيء ما يقال عليه الإفادة تصوره'. This defines the definiens as 'what is said of a thing for the purpose of conveying its concept'. The key phrase is 'الإفادة تصوره' (for conveyance of its conception).
The definition is functional: it emphasises the purpose, not the essence.
3
Distinguish two purposes of predication
Al-‘Attar explains that predication can have two goals: conveying assent (tasdiq) about the subject's state (most common), or conveying a depiction (taswir) of the subject. In definition, it is the latter. The predication here is real (haqiqi) but its essential intention is conceptualisation, not affirmation.
In 'Zayd is standing', the purpose is assent; in 'Human is rational animal', the purpose is conception.
4
Apply the distinction to an Islamic example
Consider the definition of 'wudu' in fiqh: 'Washing the face and hands and wiping the head and feet with water'. When we predicate this definition of 'wudu', we are not asserting that 'wudu is washing...' as a new fact (we already know it). Instead, the predication serves to present the concept of wudu to someone who may not know it.
The assent component (affirming the predication) is present but subordinate to the main goal of conception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمبادئ التصورات الكليَّاتُ الخمس . ومقاصدها : المعرّفُ، والقولُ الشَّارِحُ . والمصنّف لَمَّا فرغ من مباحث ومبادئ التصورات، شَرَعَ في المقاصد، فقال: [حد المعرف] ( مُعَرِّفُ الشَّيْءِ مَا يُقَالُ عَلَيْهِ ؛ أي: على الشَّيءِ الإِفَادَةِ تَصَوُّرِهِ). الدسوقي (قَوْلُهُ : فَمَبَادِئُ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ) أي : فالمبادئ التي تتحصَّلُ منها مقاصد التصورات . (قَوْلُهُ : الْكُلِّيَّاتُ الْخَمْسُ ) أي : ما عدا العرضَ العام؛ لأنَّه لا يأتي منه تعريف كما سيقول . (قَوْلُهُ : وَمَقَاصِدُهَا ) أي : المقصود؛ لأجل إفادتها. (قَوْلُهُ : الْمُعَرِّفُ وَالْقَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ ) أي : لأنَّه يقصدُ للتَّوصُّل بِهِ لِلمعرَّف، والعطفُ للتفسير. (قَوْلُهُ : لَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنْ مَبَاحِثِ وَمَبَادِئِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ) أي: لَمَّا فرغ من القضايا الَّتي يبحث فيها عن مبادئ التَّصورات، وهي الكُلِّيَّاتُ الخمس . (قَوْلُهُ : مَا يُقَالُ) أي : شيءٌ يُحملُ عليهِ حمل مواطأة؛ بأن يجعلَ الشَّيءُ موضوعاً ، والمعرَّفُ محمولاً ، وهذا شامل لحمل قائم على زيد في : زيد قائم مثلاً ، ولكنَّ قولَه : (الإفادة . . . إلخ) يخرجُهُ . العطار (قَوْلُهُ : مَبَادِئُ جَمْعُ مَبدأ ؛ بمعنى مكان البدء، وأرادَ بِهِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمس ؛ لأنَّ منها تتركَّبُ التَّعاريفُ ، فَهِيَ نَاشئةٌ عَنْهَا ، إذ الكُلُّ مُتوقِّفٌ على جُزئِهِ . (قَوْلُهُ : : مَا يُقَالُ) أي : يُحملُ عليهِ حَمْلاً حقيقيًّا، لكنَّ المقصود مِنْ ذلك الحمل التَّصويرُ ، فإِنَّ الغرضَ مِنْ حَمْل شيءٍ على شيءٍ قد يكونُ إفادةَ التَّصديقِ بحال الموضوع ، وهو الأكثر ، وقد يكونُ إفادة تصوير الموضوع بعنوان المحمول ؛ كَمَا هُنَا، وَكَما في أقسام المقولِ في جوابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ وأَيُّ شَيْءٍ هو، هذا ما اختارَهُ الدَّوَّاني وأَيَّدَهُ مير زاهد بأنَّ المقصود بالذَّاتِ مِنَ التَّعرِيفِ هُوَ تَصوُّرُ المعرَّفِ، وهذا يتصور صورة المعرّف بالكسرِ على وجه ينطبق على المعرَّف بالفتح انطباقاً بالذَّاتِ؛ كَمَا فِي تَصوُّرِ المعرِّفِ بالكنه، أو بالعرضِ كَمَا في تصوره بالوجهِ، وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّهُ حين التعريف ؛ يحملُ المعرَّفَ على المعرِّفِ ويحصلُ التَّصديق بثبوتِهِ لهُ، وإِلَّا ؛ لَمَا كانَ مرآةٌ لِمُلاحظتِهِ، لكنَّ ذلك التصديق ليس مقصوداً بِالذَّاتِ، فإنَّ القصد الواحد في الحالة الواحدة لا يمكنُ أنْ يتعلَّقَ بِالذَّاتِ بِأَمرَيْنِ كَمَا يَشْهدُ بِهِ الوجدانُ السَّليمُ
So the principles of conceptualizations are the five universals. And their goals: the definiens and the explanatory statement. When the author finished the investigations and principles of conceptualizations, he began the goals, and said: [Section on the definiens] (The definiens of a thing is what is said of it; i.e., of the thing, for the purpose of conveying its concept). Al-Dasuqi: (His statement: 'the principles of conceptualizations') means the principles from which the goals of conceptualizations are obtained. (His statement: 'the five universals') means except the common accident, because no definition comes from it as he will say. (His statement: 'and their goals') means the purpose; for the sake of conveying them. (His statement: 'the definiens and the explanatory statement') because it is intended to arrive through it at the definiendum, and the conjunction is for explanation. (His statement: 'When he finished the investigations and principles of conceptualizations') means when he finished the propositions in which he investigates the principles of conceptualizations, which are the five universals. (His statement: 'what is said') means something predicated of it with a predication of equivalency; by making the thing a subject and the definiendum a predicate, and this includes the predication of 'standing' to Zayd in 'Zayd is standing', for example, but his statement '(for the purpose of conveying its concept)... etc.' excludes it. Al-‘Attar: (His statement: 'the principles' is plural of 'mabda'' meaning place of beginning, and he intended by it the five universals because definitions are composed from them, so they arise from them, since the whole depends on its parts. (His statement: 'what is said') means predicated of it with a real predication, but the purpose of that predication is depiction, for the purpose of predicating something of something may be to convey assent regarding the state of the subject, which is most common, and may be to convey a depiction of the subject by means of the attribute of the predicate, as here, and as in the divisions of what is said in answer to: 'What is it?' and 'Which thing is it?' This is what al-Dawwani chose and Mir Zahid supported: that the essential purpose of definition is the conceptualization of the definiendum, and this is to conceive the form of the definiens (with kasr) in a way that applies to the definiendum (with fatah) with an essential application, as in conceptualizing the definiens by essence, or by accident as in conceptualizing it by aspect. And there is no doubt that during definition, the definiendum is predicated of the definiens and assent to its being established for it obtains, otherwise it would not be a mirror for observing it, but that assent is not intended essentially, for a single intention in a single state cannot be essentially related to two things, as sound intuition testifies.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage defines the 'mu'arif' (definiens) and clarifies its purpose. It opens with the author stating that the principles of conceptualizations (mabadi' al-tasawwurat) are the five universals, and the goals (maqasid) are the definiens and the explanatory statement (qawl sharih). The definition given is: 'The definiens of a thing is what is said of it for the purpose of conveying its concept.' Al-Dasuqi then explains each phrase. 'Principles' here means the sources from which the goals are derived, and the five universals are mentioned excluding the common accident because it does not yield a proper definition. The 'goals' refer to what is intended by the principles. The 'definiens' and 'explanatory statement' are synonyms (the conjunction is for explanation). The comment that the author 'finished the investigations and principles' refers to his prior discussion of the propositions about the principles (the five universals). Al-Dasuqi then clarifies that 'what is said' means a predication of equivalency (haml muwata'a), where the thing is subject and the definiendum is predicate; this includes ordinary predications like 'Zayd is standing', but the phrase 'for the purpose of conveying its concept' excludes such ordinary predications because their purpose is assent. Al-‘Attar adds that 'mabadi' (principles) is plural of mabda' (place of beginning), referring to the five universals as components from which definitions are composed. He further explains that the predication here is real (haqiqi), but its purpose is not assent but depiction (taswir). He distinguishes two purposes of predication: most commonly it is to give assent (tasdiq) about the subject's state, but here it is to depict the subject by means of the predicate. This view is chosen by al-Dawwani and supported by Mir Zahid: the essential aim is conceptualization (tasawwur) of the definiendum. The predication is indeed made, and a tacit assent occurs, but that assent is not the primary intention because a single act of intention cannot have two simultaneous essential aims. This reasoning guards against the misunderstanding that definitional predication is for affirmation; rather, it is a tool for conveying the concept. For example, when we define 'human' as 'rational animal', we predicate 'rational animal' of 'human' not to affirm that 'human is rational animal' (which would be a tautology) but to present the concept of human via its definition.

Key Terms
معرف
حمل
تصور
تصديق
قول شارح

D) Definitional predication is only for the five universals, while ordinary predication is for all categories.

Key Takeaway
The purpose of predication in a definition is to convey the concept of the definiendum, not to affirm a property.

?

Real Predication in Definition: Conception Not Affirmation
Al-Sharnubi refines the view that predication in definition is real, with full explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of real predication and explain why definitional predication is real but serves conception, not affirmation.

Core Idea
Definitional predication is real, but it conveys the concept, not a property.

When we define something, like 'Man is a rational animal,' is that a real predication? Some early scholars thought not, because the purpose is to define, not to inform. Al-Sharnubi's footnote clarifies that it is indeed real predication, but of a special kind that aims at conception. This distinction is crucial for correctly analyzing definitions in Islamic sciences, where precision affects rulings and arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Find the phrase 'القائل بعدم الحمل السيد السند' (the one who denies predication is al-Sayyid al-Sanad) and 'التحقيق ما ذهب إليه الجلال الدواني' (the verification is what al-Dawwani held). Recognize two camps: those who deny real predication and those who affirm it with refinement.
Al-Sanad thought definitional predication is only apparent.
2
Distinguish the two types of real predication
Locate the division: 'وهو قسمان ما يقصد به صفة الموضوع' (one intended for attribute of subject, e.g., 'Zayd is standing') and 'وما يقصد به تصور الموضوع بصورة المحمول' (one intended for conceiving subject in form of predicate, as in definitions). Note the different purposes: tasdiq vs. tasawwur.
The first type is abundant, the second is specific to definitions.
3
Apply the distinction to definitions
Understand that the definiendum has two aspects: individuals (أفراده) and concept (مفهومه). In definition, the concept is intended. Thus the author's phrase 'لإفادة تصوره' does not negate real predication; it specifies the type.
This resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
See the consequence of confusion
Observe that those who confused the two aspects violated Arabic grammar by positing an explicative 'i.e.' and irregular phrasing. This shows the practical importance of the distinction.
Al-Sharnubi criticizes this as unheard of except here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1) (قَوْلُهُ: وفي الحقيقة. إلخ) القائل بعدم الحمل السيد السند والتحقيق ما ذهب إليه الجلال الدواني من أن الحمل حقيقي، وهو قسمان ما يقصد به صفة الموضوع كحمل قائم على زيد وهو الكثير، وما يقصد به تصور الموضوع بصورة المحمول كما هنا من حيث انطباق التعريف على المعرّف دون نقص أو زيادة يدلّ لذلك قول جبريل للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أجابه عن حقيقة الإيمان ولا ينافي ذلك قول المصنف : لإفادة تصوره فإن الموضوع وهو المعرَّف له بالفتح جهتان أفراده ،ومفهومه، فمن جهة الحمل يراد به أفراده إذ الموضوع من حيث هو موضوع یراد به لما صدق ومن جهة كونه بصدد التفسير والتعريف يراد به المفهوم، إذ التعاريف إنما هي للمفاهيم ولما اشتبه عليهم إحدى الجهتين بالأخرى اضطربوا حتى خرجوا عن البديهي من قواعد النحو فقدروا : «أي التفسيرية ورفعوا ما بعدها بالتجرد على أن لا يكون مبتدأ ولا خبراً مما لم نسمع به إلا هنا . ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي .
(1) (His statement: 'But in reality... etc.') The one who denies predication is al-Sayyid al-Sanad, but the verification is what al-Jalal al-Dawwani went to, that the predication is real, and it is two types: one intended for the attribute of the subject, like the predication of 'standing' to Zayd, and that is abundant; and one intended for conceiving the subject in the form of the predicate, as here, in terms of the definition applying to the definiendum without deficiency or excess. Evidence for that is the statement of Jibril to the Prophet (peace be upon him): he answered him about the reality of faith. And that does not contradict the author's statement: 'for the purpose of conveying its concept', because the subject, which is the definiendum (with fatah), has two aspects: its individuals and its concept. So from the perspective of predication, its individuals are intended, because the subject as subject is intended for what it applies to. And from the perspective of its being in the context of interpretation and definition, its concept is intended, for definitions are only for concepts. When they confused the two aspects with each other, they became agitated to the extent that they left the obvious rules of grammar, and they estimated an explicative 'i.e.' and raised what follows it with 'tajarrud' so that it is neither subject nor predicate, something we have not heard of except here. End of quote. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This footnote from al-Sharnubi is a critical refinement of the earlier discussion on the nature of predication in definition. It identifies the position of al-Sayyid al-Sanad who denied that the predication is real (i.e., claimed it is merely apparent), and then presents what al-Dawwani and Mir Zahid established: the predication is indeed real (haqiqi), but it is of a specific type. Al-Dawwani divides real predication into two kinds: one intended to attribute a property to the subject, like 'Zayd is standing', where the purpose is to inform about the subject's state (tasdiq); the other intended to conceive the subject through the form of the predicate, as in definitions, where the predicate (the definiens) provides the concept of the subject (the definiendum). The footnote uses the example of Jibril asking the Prophet about the reality of faith; the answer (the definition) is a real predication that conveys the concept of faith, not merely an apparent predication. The footnote clarifies that the definiendum has two aspects: its individuals (afrad) and its concept (mafhum). In the context of definition, the intended reference is the concept, while in ordinary predication the reference is the individuals. This resolves the confusion: the author's phrase 'for the purpose of conveying its concept' does not negate real predication; it simply indicates which aspect is primary. The footnote criticizes those who mistakenly thought the predication is not real and even violated Arabic grammar by positing an explicative 'i.e.' and treating the words abnormally. This guards against the misunderstanding that definitional predication is merely formal or figurative.

Key Takeaway
Real predication in definition is genuine but directed at conceiving the definiendum, not at affirming a property — a refinement that preserves logical accuracy in Islamic scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'al-ʻilm al-qudūmi: huwa al-khabr al-mutaʻalliq bi mā kāna' (eternal knowledge is the attribute connected to what will be). Analyze whether this is a real predication of the first or second type. Justify your answer using the distinction from this lesson.

Real vs Apparent Predication in Definitions
Debate on the reality of predication in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the positions of al-Sayyid al-Sharif and al-Dawwani on predication in definitions and explain why al-Dawwani's view is considered the verified position.

Core Idea
In definitions, predication is real but its essential purpose is conceptualization, not assent.

When you say 'Man is a rational animal,' is that a real judgment or just a device to convey the meaning? This lesson unpacks the debate between two major logicians: al-Sayyid al-Sharif, who denies real predication in definitions, and al-Dawwani, who affirms it but reorients its purpose. You will learn how to tell the difference and why al-Dawwani's view prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the claim that predication in definitions is only apparent (ẓāhirī) and the counterclaim that it is real (ḥaqīqī). Note the philosophers: al-Sayyid al-Sharif vs al-Dawwānī.
The source calls al-Sayyid's view 'denial of predication'.
2
Extract the reasoning for apparent predication
The apparent-predication side argues: real predication yields assent (taṣdīq), but the author's stated goal is conceptualization (taṣawwur), so we must not intend judgment. Also, definition is about quiddity, not individuals.
They propose an explanatory 'ay' to avoid subject-predicate structure.
3
Extract al-Dawwani's argument for real predication
Al-Dawwani says real predication does occur, but the resulting assent is not the primary intention. The single mental focus is conceptualization; the judgment is a necessary byproduct. The subject has two aspects: individuals (for predication) and concept (for definition).
Al-Dawwani cites the hadith of Jibrīl and intuition to support his view.
4
Evaluate why al-Dawwani's view is 'verified'
The commentator favors al-Dawwani because his account saves the grammatical necessity of a subject-predicate structure while preserving the logical purpose of conceptualization. The alternative violates both grammar and common sense.
The passage declares al-Dawwani's view 'al-taḥqīq' (the verified position).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ. فقولُه : «ما يقالُ عليه جنس شامل للمعرف وغيره، وحمل المعرَّف على المعرّفِ حمل ظاهري؛ أي: أنَّه حمل بحسب الصورة، وفي الحقيقة ليس هناك حمل، فإذا قُلْتَ: الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق، فالإنسان في الصُّورة: موضوع، وحيوان ناطق محمول، لكن ليسَ الحُكْمُ والحَمْلُ بمراد ؛ لإفادتِهِ التَّصديق، فَيُنافي قول المصنف : لإفادة تَصوُّره، وأيضاً المحكوم عليه في الحقيقة : الأفراد، والتَّعريف للماهيَّة، فالغرضُ إِنَّما هو كشفُ الماهية وتفسيرها ، وحينئذ؛ فالمعنى على حذفِ أي التَّفسيريَّة وَقولُكَ : الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق في معنى ؛ أي: الحيوانُ النَّاطق . (قَوْلُهُ : لِلْمُعَرِّفِ وَغَيْرِهِ) كقائم من : زيدٌ قائم، وشامل للكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمس. هُنَا، وَكَما في أقسام المقولِ في جوابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ وأَيُّ شَيْءٍ هو، هذا ما اختارَهُ الدَّوَّاني وأَيَّدَهُ مير زاهد بأنَّ المقصود بالذَّاتِ مِنَ التَّعرِيفِ هُوَ تَصوُّرُ المعرَّفِ، وهذا يتصور صورة المعرّف بالكسرِ على وجه ينطبق على المعرَّف بالفتح انطباقاً بالذَّاتِ؛ كَمَا فِي تَصوُّرِ المعرِّفِ بالكنه، أو بالعرضِ كَمَا في تصوره بالوجهِ، وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّهُ حين التعريف ؛ يحملُ المعرَّفَ على المعرِّفِ ويحصلُ التَّصديق بثبوتِهِ لهُ، وإِلَّا ؛ لَمَا كانَ مرآةٌ لِمُلاحظتِهِ، لكنَّ ذلك التصديق ليس مقصوداً بِالذَّاتِ، فإنَّ القصد الواحد في الحالة الواحدة لا يمكنُ أنْ يتعلَّقَ بِالذَّاتِ بِأَمرَيْنِ كَمَا يَشْهدُ بِهِ الوجدانُ السَّليمُ. (قَوْلُهُ: وفي الحقيقة. إلخ) القائل بعدم الحمل السيد السند والتحقيق ما ذهب إليه الجلال الدواني من أن الحمل حقيقي، وهو قسمان ما يقصد به صفة الموضوع كحمل قائم على زيد وهو الكثير، وما يقصد به تصور الموضوع بصورة المحمول كما هنا من حيث انطباق التعريف على المعرّف دون نقص أو زيادة يدلّ لذلك قول جبريل للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أجابه عن حقيقة الإيمان ولا ينافي ذلك قول المصنف : لإفادة تصوره فإن الموضوع وهو المعرَّف له بالفتح جهتان أفراده ،ومفهومه، فمن جهة الحمل يراد به أفراده إذ الموضوع من حيث هو موضوع يراد به لما صدق ومن جهة كونه بصدد التفسير والتعريف يراد به المفهوم، إذ التعاريف إنما هي للمفاهيم ولما اشتبه عليهم إحدى الجهتين بالأخرى اضطربوا حتى خرجوا عن البديهي من قواعد النحو فقدروا : «أي التفسيرية ورفعوا ما بعدها بالتجرد على أن لا يكون مبتدأ ولا خبراً مما لم نسمع به إلا هنا . ونقل المحنِّي عَن السَّيِّدِ إنكار الحمل بين المعرف والمعرَّفِ، وفرَّعَ عليه أنَّا إذا قُلْنَا في جوابِ ما الإنسانُ : حيوان ناطق ؛ لا يقدَّرُ لَهُ مبتدأ ولا خبرٌ، وإِنَّما رُفِعَ؛ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا لم يكن لهُ مَا يعملُ فيهِ؛ أُعطي حركةَ الرَّفْعِ لتجرده، وهو كلام غيرُ مُستَقِيمٍ؛ لأنَّا لا نخرجُ القواعد النحويَّةَ المتكلّفة بإصلاح الألفاظ على الاصطلاحاتِ المنطقيَّةِ ، والنُّحاةُ لا يُنكرونَ الحمل، والمبتدأ عندَهُم مُقدَّرٌ في الصُّورة المذكورة، ولم يستثنهَا أحدٌ من مواضع تقدير المبتدأ أو الخبر لقيام القرينة، فالحُكْمُ عندَهُم مُطَّردٌ، وَمَا ذكرَهُ المحشّي يُوجِبُ تَخصيصاً في کلامِهِم مِنْ عِندِ نفسِهِ، وكأنَّ بعض أشياخِنَا اغتر بمثل هذا الكلام فقالَ: إنَّ مثل قولنا : الإنسان حيوان ناطق ؛ أنَّهُ على حذفِ «أي» التفسييريَّةِ، وتَعليلُ الرَّفْعِ بِمَا ذكَرَ مُخالفٌ لِمَا أجمعُوا عليهِ مِنْ أَنَّ الرَّفعَ بالتَّجرُّدِ مُختصّ بالمضارع؛ مَعَ لزومِ أَنْ يكونَ الأسماء قبلَ التَّركيب كلها مرفوعةً بِمُقتَضَى هذا التعليل، قالَ الدَّوَّاني : ومنْ أراد المحافظة على ما قرَّرَهُ بعضُ المتأخّرينَ مِن انتفاء الحمل ؛ فَلَهُ أنْ يقول : المرادُ بِمَا يُقالُ عليه ما من شأنه أن يحمل عليهِ؛ إلا أنَّ عدَّهم الحدَّ بالنسبة إلى المحدود؛ من أصناف المقول في جواب ما هو، مع تفسيرهم المقول بالمحمول؛ يوجبُ كونَ الحدّ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ حدٌ ؛ مقولاً وَمَحمولاً على محدودِهِ، وهذا خادش لِمَا قرَّرَهُ بعضُهُمْ مِنَ انتفاء الحمل في التَّعريف . وقَولُهُ: مَا مِنْ شَأْنِهِ أَنْ يحمل عليهِ؛ أي: لا في حالِ التَّعريفِ، وَمَا تعقَّبَ بِهِ المحشّي كلامَهُ بأَنَّ قولَهُ: مَا مِنْ شأنه ... إلخ؛ يلزمُ عليهِ جعلَ التَّعريف شاملاً لأغيارٍ أكثرَ مِن أنْ تُحصَى؛ مَدفوع بخروج هذه الأغيار بقيد لإفادة تصورِهِ، وأمَّا حمل تلك الأغيار لا في حالِ التَّعريف ؛ فإنَّما تفيدُ التَّصديق دونَ التَّصورِ، قالَ العصامُ: وَمِمَّا يؤيّدُ اعتبار الحمل في التَّعريف؛ أنَّ تركيب لفظي المعرّفِ والمعرَّف ؛ تركيب تام، وليس داخلاً في شيء من أقسام الإنشاء، فَلَا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ تَركيباً خبريًّا مُشتَمِلاً على الحُكم
Section: On the definition and its divisions. His statement: 'What is said upon it is a genus including the definer and other things.' The predication of the definiendum on the definer is apparent predication; that is, it is predication in form, but in reality there is no predication. So if you say: 'Man is a rational animal,' then 'man' in form is a subject, and 'rational animal' is a predicate, but the judgment and predication are not intended because they would give assent (tasdiq), contradicting the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it.' Also, what is judged upon in reality is the individuals, while the definition is for the quiddity; thus the purpose is only to unveil the quiddity and interpret it. Therefore, the meaning involves the deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and your saying 'Man is a rational animal' means 'the rational animal.' His statement: 'for the definer and other things' like 'standing' in 'Zayd is standing,' and it includes the five universals. Here, as in the divisions of what is said in answer to 'What is it?' and 'Which thing is it?' This is what al-Dawwani chose and Mir Zahid supported: that the primary purpose of definition is conceptualization of the definiendum, and this conceptualizes the form of the definer such that it applies to the definiendum essentially, as in conceptualizing the definer by its essence, or accidentally as in conceptualizing by its aspect. There is no doubt that during definition, the definiendum is predicated on the definer and assent to its being true for it occurs; otherwise it would not be a mirror for observing it. But that assent is not intended essentially, for a single intention in a single state cannot essentially relate to two things, as sound intuition testifies. (His statement: 'In reality, etc.') The one who denies predication is al-Sayyid al-Sanad, but the verified position is what al-Jalal al-Dawwani went to: that predication is real, and it is of two types: one intended to describe the subject, like the predication of 'standing' on Zayd, which is common; and one intended to conceptualize the subject through the form of the predicate, as here, in terms of the definition's application to the definiendum without deficiency or excess. This is supported by the saying of Jibril to the Prophet (PBUH) when he answered about the reality of faith. And this does not conflict with the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', because the subject, which is the definiendum, has two aspects: its individuals and its concept. From the aspect of predication, its individuals are intended, since the subject as subject is intended for what it applies to; and from the aspect of interpretation and definition, the concept is intended, since definitions are for concepts. When they confused these two aspects, they became confused and even went against the obvious rules of grammar, positing the explanatory 'ay' and raising what follows it due to being devoid of an operator, such that it is neither subject nor predicate - something unheard of except here. Al-Muḥannī narrated from al-Sayyid the denial of predication between the definer and the definiendum, and branched from it that if we say in answer to 'What is man?' 'Rational animal', there is neither a subject nor a predicate estimated, rather it is raised because when nothing operates on it, it is given the case of raf' due to its being devoid of an operator. This is unsound, because we do not discard grammatical rules forced to reform expressions for logical terminologies. Grammarians do not deny predication; for them, a subject is estimated in the mentioned form, and no one has excluded it from cases of estimating a subject or predicate due to the presence of a contextual clue; their rule is universal. What the commentator (al-Muḥannī) mentioned would necessitate a specification in their rules from himself. It seems that some of our teachers were deceived by such speech, saying that a statement like 'Man is a rational animal' involves deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and the explanation of raf' by what was mentioned contradicts their consensus that raf' due to being devoid of an operator is specific to the imperfect verb (mudári'), and it would also entail that nouns before composition are all in the nominative case according to this reasoning. Al-Dawwani said: Whoever wants to preserve what some later scholars established of the negation of predication can say: 'What is said upon it' means 'what is apt to be predicated upon it', except that their counting of the definition (hadd) with respect to the defined as one of the categories of what is said in answer to 'What is it?', along with their interpretation of 'what is said' as 'the predicate', necessitates that the definition as a definition is a predicate of the defined, which undermines the negation of predication in definition. His statement: 'what is apt to be predicated upon it' means not at the time of definition. The objection by the commentator (al-Muḥannī) against his statement that 'what is apt... etc.' would entail making the definition include countless other things; this is refuted by the fact that those other things are excluded by the condition 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', and the predication of those other things not in the state of definition only yields assent, not conceptualization. Al-Isam said: Among the things that support the consideration of predication in definition is that the verbal combination of the definer and the definiendum is a complete combination, and it does not fall under any category of non-informative (insha) constructions; thus it must be an informative (khabari) construction containing a judgment.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the nature of predication (haml) in definitions (ta'rīf). It opens by quoting the matn statement 'What is said upon it (ma yqalu 'alayh) is a genus including the definer and other things.' The commentator then explains that some logicians, like al-Sayyid al-Sharif, hold that predication in definitions is only apparent, not real. For instance, if you say 'Man is a rational animal' (al-insānu hayawānun nāṭiqun), in form 'man' is subject and 'rational animal' is predicate, but in reality no judgment is intended because the purpose is conceptualization (tasawwur), not assent (tasdiq). If it were real predication, it would give assent, contradicting the author's aim. Moreover, in reality, what is judged are the individuals, whereas definitions are of quiddities, so the meaning is like 'the rational animal' with an implied explanatory 'ay' (i.e., 'i.e.'). The passage then presents al-Dawwānī's view, supported by Mīr Zāhid, that the primary purpose of definition is indeed conceptualization of the definiendum, but this conceptualization requires a real predication, though the resulting assent is not the essential aim. The subject has two aspects: individuals (afrād) and concept (mafhūm). In predication, we consider the individuals (the subjects of judgment), but in definition we consider the concept. Confusion between these led some to violate grammatical rules by positing an explanatory 'ay' and denying subject-predicate structure. The commentator refutes the denial of predication, arguing that grammarians universally accept an estimated subject in such constructions. Al-Dawwānī further argues that if one wants to avoid predication in definition, they can interpret 'ma yqalu 'alayh' as 'what is apt to be predicated', but this is undermined by the fact that definitions are counted among the categories of answers to 'what is it?', which are predicates. Finally, al-‘Isām supports predication by noting that the combination of definer and definiendum is a complete informative (khabarī) sentence, not an exclamatory or interrogative one, so it must contain a judgment. Throughout, the text uses examples like 'Zayd is standing' and 'Man is a rational animal', and references the hadith of Jibrīl regarding faith. The overall argument is that real predication occurs in definitions, but the primary cognitive purpose is conceptualization, not assent.

Checkpoint
According to al-Dawwānī's position presented in the passage, what is the primary purpose of the predication in a definition like 'Man is a rational animal'?
A) To produce a judgment about the existence of man.
B) To conceptualize the definiendum (man).
C) To affirm that the definer (rational animal) describes man.
D) To deny the reality of the subject.

Key Takeaway
Predication in definitions is real, but its essential function is to enable conceptualization, not to produce a separate judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a definition from an Uṣūl al-Fiqh textbook (e.g., 'al-ʿilla is what necessitates the ḥukm'). State whether the predication is real or apparent according to al-Dawwani's criterion. Explain why.
?
Take the qiyās (analogy) example: 'Wine is forbidden because of its intoxication. Everything intoxicating is like wine.' Identify the definition involved and discuss whether predication in the major premise is real or apparent.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
10 min
The Two Aspects of the Subject in Definitions
Clarifying the two aspects of the definiendum to resolve confusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two aspects (individuals and concept) of the subject in a definition and explain how confusion between them led to grammatical violations.

Core Idea
Confusing the individual and conceptual aspects of the definiendum leads to errors in logic and grammar.

The word 'man' in 'Man is a rational animal' can refer either to the individuals that are men or to the concept of manhood. This lesson shows how failing to distinguish these aspects causes some logicians to deny predication altogether and to violate standard Arabic grammar. You will learn to keep these aspects separate, a skill crucial for accurate definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two aspects of the definiendum
The passage states that the definiendum (muʿarraf) has two aspects: its individuals (afrād) and its concept (mafhūm). In the sentence 'Man is a rational animal', when considered as a subject of predication, 'man' refers to individuals; when considered as something to be defined, it refers to the concept.
Al-Dawwānī uses this distinction to reconcile real predication with conceptualization.
2
Trace the confusion that leads to denying predication
Some later logicians confused the two aspects: they saw that definitions are about concepts, so they thought 'man' in the definition must be the concept, not the individuals. Since a concept cannot really be predicated on individuals (or vice versa), they concluded the predication is only apparent.
This confusion led them to violate grammatical rules by positing an explanatory 'ay' and denying a subject-predicate structure.
3
See how al-Dawwani resolves the confusion
Al-Dawwānī keeps the two aspects distinct: in the very same sentence, from the angle of predication, 'man' refers to individuals (the subject of assent); from the angle of definition, it refers to the concept. Both are valid; there is no need to delete or reinterpret the sentence.
The real predication applies to individuals, but the cognitive aim is to grasp the concept.
4
Apply the distinction to an example from fiqh
Consider the definition of 'zakāt' as 'a specific amount of wealth given to specified recipients'. If you say 'Zakāt is a specific amount...', does 'zakāt' refer to the individuals (the actual wealth) or the concept? The distinction helps clarify which aspect is being defined.
This prevents mistakes when using definitions in legal arguments.

فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ. فقولُه : «ما يقالُ عليه جنس شامل للمعرف وغيره، وحمل المعرَّف على المعرّفِ حمل ظاهري؛ أي: أنَّه حمل بحسب الصورة، وفي الحقيقة ليس هناك حمل، فإذا قُلْتَ: الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق، فالإنسان في الصُّورة: موضوع، وحيوان ناطق محمول، لكن ليسَ الحُكْمُ والحَمْلُ بمراد ؛ لإفادتِهِ التَّصديق، فَيُنافي قول المصنف : لإفادة تَصوُّره، وأيضاً المحكوم عليه في الحقيقة : الأفراد، والتَّعريف للماهيَّة، فالغرضُ إِنَّما هو كشفُ الماهية وتفسيرها ، وحينئذ؛ فالمعنى على حذفِ أي التَّفسيريَّة وَقولُكَ : الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق في معنى ؛ أي: الحيوانُ النَّاطق . (قَوْلُهُ : لِلْمُعَرِّفِ وَغَيْرِهِ) كقائم من : زيدٌ قائم، وشامل للكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمس. هُنَا، وَكَما في أقسام المقولِ في جوابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ وأَيُّ شَيْءٍ هو، هذا ما اختارَهُ الدَّوَّاني وأَيَّدَهُ مير زاهد بأنَّ المقصود بالذَّاتِ مِنَ التَّعرِيفِ هُوَ تَصوُّرُ المعرَّفِ، وهذا يتصور صورة المعرّف بالكسرِ على وجه ينطبق على المعرَّف بالفتح انطباقاً بالذَّاتِ؛ كَمَا فِي تَصوُّرِ المعرِّفِ بالكنه، أو بالعرضِ كَمَا في تصوره بالوجهِ، وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّهُ حين التعريف ؛ يحملُ المعرَّفَ على المعرِّفِ ويحصلُ التَّصديق بثبوتِهِ لهُ، وإِلَّا ؛ لَمَا كانَ مرآةٌ لِمُلاحظتِهِ، لكنَّ ذلك التصديق ليس مقصوداً بِالذَّاتِ، فإنَّ القصد الواحد في الحالة الواحدة لا يمكنُ أنْ يتعلَّقَ بِالذَّاتِ بِأَمرَيْنِ كَمَا يَشْهدُ بِهِ الوجدانُ السَّليمُ. (قَوْلُهُ: وفي الحقيقة. إلخ) القائل بعدم الحمل السيد السند والتحقيق ما ذهب إليه الجلال الدواني من أن الحمل حقيقي، وهو قسمان ما يقصد به صفة الموضوع كحمل قائم على زيد وهو الكثير، وما يقصد به تصور الموضوع بصورة المحمول كما هنا من حيث انطباق التعريف على المعرّف دون نقص أو زيادة يدلّ لذلك قول جبريل للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أجابه عن حقيقة الإيمان ولا ينافي ذلك قول المصنف : لإفادة تصوره فإن الموضوع وهو المعرَّف له بالفتح جهتان أفراده ،ومفهومه، فمن جهة الحمل يراد به أفراده إذ الموضوع من حيث هو موضوع يراد به لما صدق ومن جهة كونه بصدد التفسير والتعريف يراد به المفهوم، إذ التعاريف إنما هي للمفاهيم ولما اشتبه عليهم إحدى الجهتين بالأخرى اضطربوا حتى خرجوا عن البديهي من قواعد النحو فقدروا : «أي التفسيرية ورفعوا ما بعدها بالتجرد على أن لا يكون مبتدأ ولا خبراً مما لم نسمع به إلا هنا . ونقل المحنِّي عَن السَّيِّدِ إنكار الحمل بين المعرف والمعرَّفِ، وفرَّعَ عليه أنَّا إذا قُلْنَا في جوابِ ما الإنسانُ : حيوان ناطق ؛ لا يقدَّرُ لَهُ مبتدأ ولا خبرٌ، وإِنَّما رُفِعَ؛ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا لم يكن لهُ مَا يعملُ فيهِ؛ أُعطي حركةَ الرَّفْعِ لتجرده، وهو كلام غيرُ مُستَقِيمٍ؛ لأنَّا لا نخرجُ القواعد النحويَّةَ المتكلّفة بإصلاح الألفاظ على الاصطلاحاتِ المنطقيَّةِ ، والنُّحاةُ لا يُنكرونَ الحمل، والمبتدأ عندَهُم مُقدَّرٌ في الصُّورة المذكورة، ولم يستثنهَا أحدٌ من مواضع تقدير المبتدأ أو الخبر لقيام القرينة، فالحُكْمُ عندَهُم مُطَّردٌ، وَمَا ذكرَهُ المحشّي يُوجِبُ تَخصيصاً في کلامِهِم مِنْ عِندِ نفسِهِ، وكأنَّ بعض أشياخِنَا اغتر بمثل هذا الكلام فقالَ: إنَّ مثل قولنا : الإنسان حيوان ناطق ؛ أنَّهُ على حذفِ «أي» التفسييريَّةِ، وتَعليلُ الرَّفْعِ بِمَا ذكَرَ مُخالفٌ لِمَا أجمعُوا عليهِ مِنْ أَنَّ الرَّفعَ بالتَّجرُّدِ مُختصّ بالمضارع؛ مَعَ لزومِ أَنْ يكونَ الأسماء قبلَ التَّركيب كلها مرفوعةً بِمُقتَضَى هذا التعليل، قالَ الدَّوَّاني : ومنْ أراد المحافظة على ما قرَّرَهُ بعضُ المتأخّرينَ مِن انتفاء الحمل ؛ فَلَهُ أنْ يقول : المرادُ بِمَا يُقالُ عليه ما من شأنه أن يحمل عليهِ؛ إلا أنَّ عدَّهم الحدَّ بالنسبة إلى المحدود؛ من أصناف المقول في جواب ما هو، مع تفسيرهم المقول بالمحمول؛ يوجبُ كونَ الحدّ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ حدٌ ؛ مقولاً وَمَحمولاً على محدودِهِ، وهذا خادش لِمَا قرَّرَهُ بعضُهُمْ مِنَ انتفاء الحمل في التَّعريف . وقَولُهُ: مَا مِنْ شَأْنِهِ أَنْ يحمل عليهِ؛ أي: لا في حالِ التَّعريفِ، وَمَا تعقَّبَ بِهِ المحشّي كلامَهُ بأَنَّ قولَهُ: مَا مِنْ شأنه ... إلخ؛ يلزمُ عليهِ جعلَ التَّعريف شاملاً لأغيارٍ أكثرَ مِن أنْ تُحصَى؛ مَدفوع بخروج هذه الأغيار بقيد لإفادة تصورِهِ، وأمَّا حمل تلك الأغيار لا في حالِ التَّعريف ؛ فإنَّما تفيدُ التَّصديق دونَ التَّصورِ، قالَ العصامُ: وَمِمَّا يؤيّدُ اعتبار الحمل في التَّعريف؛ أنَّ تركيب لفظي المعرّفِ والمعرَّف ؛ تركيب تام، وليس داخلاً في شيء من أقسام الإنشاء، فَلَا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ تَركيباً خبريًّا مُشتَمِلاً على الحُكم
Section: On the definition and its divisions. His statement: 'What is said upon it is a genus including the definer and other things.' The predication of the definiendum on the definer is apparent predication; that is, it is predication in form, but in reality there is no predication. So if you say: 'Man is a rational animal,' then 'man' in form is a subject, and 'rational animal' is a predicate, but the judgment and predication are not intended because they would give assent (tasdiq), contradicting the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it.' Also, what is judged upon in reality is the individuals, while the definition is for the quiddity; thus the purpose is only to unveil the quiddity and interpret it. Therefore, the meaning involves the deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and your saying 'Man is a rational animal' means 'the rational animal.' His statement: 'for the definer and other things' like 'standing' in 'Zayd is standing,' and it includes the five universals. Here, as in the divisions of what is said in answer to 'What is it?' and 'Which thing is it?' This is what al-Dawwani chose and Mir Zahid supported: that the primary purpose of definition is conceptualization of the definiendum, and this conceptualizes the form of the definer such that it applies to the definiendum essentially, as in conceptualizing the definer by its essence, or accidentally as in conceptualizing by its aspect. There is no doubt that during definition, the definiendum is predicated on the definer and assent to its being true for it occurs; otherwise it would not be a mirror for observing it. But that assent is not intended essentially, for a single intention in a single state cannot essentially relate to two things, as sound intuition testifies. (His statement: 'In reality, etc.') The one who denies predication is al-Sayyid al-Sanad, but the verified position is what al-Jalal al-Dawwani went to: that predication is real, and it is of two types: one intended to describe the subject, like the predication of 'standing' on Zayd, which is common; and one intended to conceptualize the subject through the form of the predicate, as here, in terms of the definition's application to the definiendum without deficiency or excess. This is supported by the saying of Jibril to the Prophet (PBUH) when he answered about the reality of faith. And this does not conflict with the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', because the subject, which is the definiendum, has two aspects: its individuals and its concept. From the aspect of predication, its individuals are intended, since the subject as subject is intended for what it applies to; and from the aspect of interpretation and definition, the concept is intended, since definitions are for concepts. When they confused these two aspects, they became confused and even went against the obvious rules of grammar, positing the explanatory 'ay' and raising what follows it due to being devoid of an operator, such that it is neither subject nor predicate - something unheard of except here. Al-Muḥannī narrated from al-Sayyid the denial of predication between the definer and the definiendum, and branched from it that if we say in answer to 'What is man?' 'Rational animal', there is neither a subject nor a predicate estimated, rather it is raised because when nothing operates on it, it is given the case of raf' due to its being devoid of an operator. This is unsound, because we do not discard grammatical rules forced to reform expressions for logical terminologies. Grammarians do not deny predication; for them, a subject is estimated in the mentioned form, and no one has excluded it from cases of estimating a subject or predicate due to the presence of a contextual clue; their rule is universal. What the commentator (al-Muḥannī) mentioned would necessitate a specification in their rules from himself. It seems that some of our teachers were deceived by such speech, saying that a statement like 'Man is a rational animal' involves deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and the explanation of raf' by what was mentioned contradicts their consensus that raf' due to being devoid of an operator is specific to the imperfect verb (mudári'), and it would also entail that nouns before composition are all in the nominative case according to this reasoning. Al-Dawwani said: Whoever wants to preserve what some later scholars established of the negation of predication can say: 'What is said upon it' means 'what is apt to be predicated upon it', except that their counting of the definition (hadd) with respect to the defined as one of the categories of what is said in answer to 'What is it?', along with their interpretation of 'what is said' as 'the predicate', necessitates that the definition as a definition is a predicate of the defined, which undermines the negation of predication in definition. His statement: 'what is apt to be predicated upon it' means not at the time of definition. The objection by the commentator (al-Muḥannī) against his statement that 'what is apt... etc.' would entail making the definition include countless other things; this is refuted by the fact that those other things are excluded by the condition 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', and the predication of those other things not in the state of definition only yields assent, not conceptualization. Al-Isam said: Among the things that support the consideration of predication in definition is that the verbal combination of the definer and the definiendum is a complete combination, and it does not fall under any category of non-informative (insha) constructions; thus it must be an informative (khabari) construction containing a judgment.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the nature of predication (haml) in definitions (ta'rīf). It opens by quoting the matn statement 'What is said upon it (ma yqalu 'alayh) is a genus including the definer and other things.' The commentator then explains that some logicians, like al-Sayyid al-Sharif, hold that predication in definitions is only apparent, not real. For instance, if you say 'Man is a rational animal' (al-insānu hayawānun nāṭiqun), in form 'man' is subject and 'rational animal' is predicate, but in reality no judgment is intended because the purpose is conceptualization (tasawwur), not assent (tasdiq). If it were real predication, it would give assent, contradicting the author's aim. Moreover, in reality, what is judged are the individuals, whereas definitions are of quiddities, so the meaning is like 'the rational animal' with an implied explanatory 'ay' (i.e., 'i.e.'). The passage then presents al-Dawwānī's view, supported by Mīr Zāhid, that the primary purpose of definition is indeed conceptualization of the definiendum, but this conceptualization requires a real predication, though the resulting assent is not the essential aim. The subject has two aspects: individuals (afrād) and concept (mafhūm). In predication, we consider the individuals (the subjects of judgment), but in definition we consider the concept. Confusion between these led some to violate grammatical rules by positing an explanatory 'ay' and denying subject-predicate structure. The commentator refutes the denial of predication, arguing that grammarians universally accept an estimated subject in such constructions. Al-Dawwānī further argues that if one wants to avoid predication in definition, they can interpret 'ma yqalu 'alayh' as 'what is apt to be predicated', but this is undermined by the fact that definitions are counted among the categories of answers to 'what is it?', which are predicates. Finally, al-‘Isām supports predication by noting that the combination of definer and definiendum is a complete informative (khabarī) sentence, not an exclamatory or interrogative one, so it must contain a judgment. Throughout, the text uses examples like 'Zayd is standing' and 'Man is a rational animal', and references the hadith of Jibrīl regarding faith. The overall argument is that real predication occurs in definitions, but the primary cognitive purpose is conceptualization, not assent.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two aspects does the subject in a definition like 'Man is a rational animal' have?
A) Substance and accident.
B) Individuals (afrād) and concept (mafhūm).
C) Genus and differentia.
D) Definer and defined.

Key Takeaway
Keeping the two aspects of the subject separate resolves the apparent conflict between real predication and the conceptual purpose of definition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take the definition 'al-ʿālam is everything other than Allāh'. Identify the two aspects of 'al-ʿālam' (individuals: all created things; concept: the meaning of world). Explain how the predication works differently for each aspect.
?
In a debate about the definition of 'ʿilla' (cause), a grammarian objects that the definition 'ʿilla is that on which a ruling depends' cannot be a real predication. Using the two-aspect analysis, respond to the objection.

Hadd and Rasm
advanced
10 min
Grammatical Grounding of Predication in Definitions
Grammatical refutation of the denial of predication in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to refute the denial of predication in definitions using standard Arabic grammatical rules and explain why 'Man is a rational animal' is a genuine khabari sentence.

Core Idea
The definitional sentence is a complete informative construction, necessarily containing a judgment, as supported by universal grammatical rules.

Some logicians, to salvage the conceptual purpose of definition, claimed that sentences like 'Man is a rational animal' are not real subject-predicate sentences. This lesson uses the authority of Arabic grammar to demolish that claim. You will see why even the most sophisticated logical revision cannot overrule the plain structure of Arabic speech, and how this reinforces the reality of predication in definitions.

Guided Path
1
State the denial position and its grammatical consequence
Al-Muḥannī reports that al-Sayyid denied any real predication in definitions. Therefore, in 'Man is a rational animal', neither a subject nor a predicate is estimated; the rafʿ case on 'rational animal' is due to its being devoid of an operator (tajarud).
This is a radical departure from standard Arabic syntax.
2
Refute the denial using universal grammatical rules
The commentator argues: Grammarians universally accept that such sentences have an estimated subject (mubtadaʾ) because a contextual clue exists. The rule of rafʿ by tajarud is specific to the imperfect verb, not to nouns. If it applied to nouns, then all isolated nouns would be nominative before composition, which is absurd.
This shows the denial violates established grammatical principles.
3
Present al-Dawwani's refined position
Al-Dawwānī offers a way for those who still reject predication: interpret 'ma yqalu ʿalayh' as 'what is apt to be predicated', not 'what is actually predicated in the definition'. But he notes this fails because definitions are considered predicates in answers to 'What is it?'.
The commentator and al-ʿIṣām ultimately dismiss this as unnecessary.
4
Show the final argument from construction type
Al-ʿIṣām concludes: The combination of definer and definiendum is a complete combination (tarkīb tāmm). It does not fall under any inshāʾ (non-informative) category. Therefore it must be khabarī (informative) and contain a judgment (ḥukm). This proves real predication.
This argument anchors predication in the very nature of Arabic sentences.

فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ. فقولُه : «ما يقالُ عليه جنس شامل للمعرف وغيره، وحمل المعرَّف على المعرّفِ حمل ظاهري؛ أي: أنَّه حمل بحسب الصورة، وفي الحقيقة ليس هناك حمل، فإذا قُلْتَ: الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق، فالإنسان في الصُّورة: موضوع، وحيوان ناطق محمول، لكن ليسَ الحُكْمُ والحَمْلُ بمراد ؛ لإفادتِهِ التَّصديق، فَيُنافي قول المصنف : لإفادة تَصوُّره، وأيضاً المحكوم عليه في الحقيقة : الأفراد، والتَّعريف للماهيَّة، فالغرضُ إِنَّما هو كشفُ الماهية وتفسيرها ، وحينئذ؛ فالمعنى على حذفِ أي التَّفسيريَّة وَقولُكَ : الإنسانُ حيوان ناطق في معنى ؛ أي: الحيوانُ النَّاطق . (قَوْلُهُ : لِلْمُعَرِّفِ وَغَيْرِهِ) كقائم من : زيدٌ قائم، وشامل للكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمس. هُنَا، وَكَما في أقسام المقولِ في جوابِ : مَا هُوَ؟ وأَيُّ شَيْءٍ هو، هذا ما اختارَهُ الدَّوَّاني وأَيَّدَهُ مير زاهد بأنَّ المقصود بالذَّاتِ مِنَ التَّعرِيفِ هُوَ تَصوُّرُ المعرَّفِ، وهذا يتصور صورة المعرّف بالكسرِ على وجه ينطبق على المعرَّف بالفتح انطباقاً بالذَّاتِ؛ كَمَا فِي تَصوُّرِ المعرِّفِ بالكنه، أو بالعرضِ كَمَا في تصوره بالوجهِ، وَلَا شَكٍّ أَنَّهُ حين التعريف ؛ يحملُ المعرَّفَ على المعرِّفِ ويحصلُ التَّصديق بثبوتِهِ لهُ، وإِلَّا ؛ لَمَا كانَ مرآةٌ لِمُلاحظتِهِ، لكنَّ ذلك التصديق ليس مقصوداً بِالذَّاتِ، فإنَّ القصد الواحد في الحالة الواحدة لا يمكنُ أنْ يتعلَّقَ بِالذَّاتِ بِأَمرَيْنِ كَمَا يَشْهدُ بِهِ الوجدانُ السَّليمُ. (قَوْلُهُ: وفي الحقيقة. إلخ) القائل بعدم الحمل السيد السند والتحقيق ما ذهب إليه الجلال الدواني من أن الحمل حقيقي، وهو قسمان ما يقصد به صفة الموضوع كحمل قائم على زيد وهو الكثير، وما يقصد به تصور الموضوع بصورة المحمول كما هنا من حيث انطباق التعريف على المعرّف دون نقص أو زيادة يدلّ لذلك قول جبريل للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أجابه عن حقيقة الإيمان ولا ينافي ذلك قول المصنف : لإفادة تصوره فإن الموضوع وهو المعرَّف له بالفتح جهتان أفراده ،ومفهومه، فمن جهة الحمل يراد به أفراده إذ الموضوع من حيث هو موضوع يراد به لما صدق ومن جهة كونه بصدد التفسير والتعريف يراد به المفهوم، إذ التعاريف إنما هي للمفاهيم ولما اشتبه عليهم إحدى الجهتين بالأخرى اضطربوا حتى خرجوا عن البديهي من قواعد النحو فقدروا : «أي التفسيرية ورفعوا ما بعدها بالتجرد على أن لا يكون مبتدأ ولا خبراً مما لم نسمع به إلا هنا . ونقل المحنِّي عَن السَّيِّدِ إنكار الحمل بين المعرف والمعرَّفِ، وفرَّعَ عليه أنَّا إذا قُلْنَا في جوابِ ما الإنسانُ : حيوان ناطق ؛ لا يقدَّرُ لَهُ مبتدأ ولا خبرٌ، وإِنَّما رُفِعَ؛ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا لم يكن لهُ مَا يعملُ فيهِ؛ أُعطي حركةَ الرَّفْعِ لتجرده، وهو كلام غيرُ مُستَقِيمٍ؛ لأنَّا لا نخرجُ القواعد النحويَّةَ المتكلّفة بإصلاح الألفاظ على الاصطلاحاتِ المنطقيَّةِ ، والنُّحاةُ لا يُنكرونَ الحمل، والمبتدأ عندَهُم مُقدَّرٌ في الصُّورة المذكورة، ولم يستثنهَا أحدٌ من مواضع تقدير المبتدأ أو الخبر لقيام القرينة، فالحُكْمُ عندَهُم مُطَّردٌ، وَمَا ذكرَهُ المحشّي يُوجِبُ تَخصيصاً في کلامِهِم مِنْ عِندِ نفسِهِ، وكأنَّ بعض أشياخِنَا اغتر بمثل هذا الكلام فقالَ: إنَّ مثل قولنا : الإنسان حيوان ناطق ؛ أنَّهُ على حذفِ «أي» التفسييريَّةِ، وتَعليلُ الرَّفْعِ بِمَا ذكَرَ مُخالفٌ لِمَا أجمعُوا عليهِ مِنْ أَنَّ الرَّفعَ بالتَّجرُّدِ مُختصّ بالمضارع؛ مَعَ لزومِ أَنْ يكونَ الأسماء قبلَ التَّركيب كلها مرفوعةً بِمُقتَضَى هذا التعليل، قالَ الدَّوَّاني : ومنْ أراد المحافظة على ما قرَّرَهُ بعضُ المتأخّرينَ مِن انتفاء الحمل ؛ فَلَهُ أنْ يقول : المرادُ بِمَا يُقالُ عليه ما من شأنه أن يحمل عليهِ؛ إلا أنَّ عدَّهم الحدَّ بالنسبة إلى المحدود؛ من أصناف المقول في جواب ما هو، مع تفسيرهم المقول بالمحمول؛ يوجبُ كونَ الحدّ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ حدٌ ؛ مقولاً وَمَحمولاً على محدودِهِ، وهذا خادش لِمَا قرَّرَهُ بعضُهُمْ مِنَ انتفاء الحمل في التَّعريف . وقَولُهُ: مَا مِنْ شَأْنِهِ أَنْ يحمل عليهِ؛ أي: لا في حالِ التَّعريفِ، وَمَا تعقَّبَ بِهِ المحشّي كلامَهُ بأَنَّ قولَهُ: مَا مِنْ شأنه ... إلخ؛ يلزمُ عليهِ جعلَ التَّعريف شاملاً لأغيارٍ أكثرَ مِن أنْ تُحصَى؛ مَدفوع بخروج هذه الأغيار بقيد لإفادة تصورِهِ، وأمَّا حمل تلك الأغيار لا في حالِ التَّعريف ؛ فإنَّما تفيدُ التَّصديق دونَ التَّصورِ، قالَ العصامُ: وَمِمَّا يؤيّدُ اعتبار الحمل في التَّعريف؛ أنَّ تركيب لفظي المعرّفِ والمعرَّف ؛ تركيب تام، وليس داخلاً في شيء من أقسام الإنشاء، فَلَا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ تَركيباً خبريًّا مُشتَمِلاً على الحُكم
Section: On the definition and its divisions. His statement: 'What is said upon it is a genus including the definer and other things.' The predication of the definiendum on the definer is apparent predication; that is, it is predication in form, but in reality there is no predication. So if you say: 'Man is a rational animal,' then 'man' in form is a subject, and 'rational animal' is a predicate, but the judgment and predication are not intended because they would give assent (tasdiq), contradicting the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it.' Also, what is judged upon in reality is the individuals, while the definition is for the quiddity; thus the purpose is only to unveil the quiddity and interpret it. Therefore, the meaning involves the deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and your saying 'Man is a rational animal' means 'the rational animal.' His statement: 'for the definer and other things' like 'standing' in 'Zayd is standing,' and it includes the five universals. Here, as in the divisions of what is said in answer to 'What is it?' and 'Which thing is it?' This is what al-Dawwani chose and Mir Zahid supported: that the primary purpose of definition is conceptualization of the definiendum, and this conceptualizes the form of the definer such that it applies to the definiendum essentially, as in conceptualizing the definer by its essence, or accidentally as in conceptualizing by its aspect. There is no doubt that during definition, the definiendum is predicated on the definer and assent to its being true for it occurs; otherwise it would not be a mirror for observing it. But that assent is not intended essentially, for a single intention in a single state cannot essentially relate to two things, as sound intuition testifies. (His statement: 'In reality, etc.') The one who denies predication is al-Sayyid al-Sanad, but the verified position is what al-Jalal al-Dawwani went to: that predication is real, and it is of two types: one intended to describe the subject, like the predication of 'standing' on Zayd, which is common; and one intended to conceptualize the subject through the form of the predicate, as here, in terms of the definition's application to the definiendum without deficiency or excess. This is supported by the saying of Jibril to the Prophet (PBUH) when he answered about the reality of faith. And this does not conflict with the author's statement 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', because the subject, which is the definiendum, has two aspects: its individuals and its concept. From the aspect of predication, its individuals are intended, since the subject as subject is intended for what it applies to; and from the aspect of interpretation and definition, the concept is intended, since definitions are for concepts. When they confused these two aspects, they became confused and even went against the obvious rules of grammar, positing the explanatory 'ay' and raising what follows it due to being devoid of an operator, such that it is neither subject nor predicate - something unheard of except here. Al-Muḥannī narrated from al-Sayyid the denial of predication between the definer and the definiendum, and branched from it that if we say in answer to 'What is man?' 'Rational animal', there is neither a subject nor a predicate estimated, rather it is raised because when nothing operates on it, it is given the case of raf' due to its being devoid of an operator. This is unsound, because we do not discard grammatical rules forced to reform expressions for logical terminologies. Grammarians do not deny predication; for them, a subject is estimated in the mentioned form, and no one has excluded it from cases of estimating a subject or predicate due to the presence of a contextual clue; their rule is universal. What the commentator (al-Muḥannī) mentioned would necessitate a specification in their rules from himself. It seems that some of our teachers were deceived by such speech, saying that a statement like 'Man is a rational animal' involves deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and the explanation of raf' by what was mentioned contradicts their consensus that raf' due to being devoid of an operator is specific to the imperfect verb (mudári'), and it would also entail that nouns before composition are all in the nominative case according to this reasoning. Al-Dawwani said: Whoever wants to preserve what some later scholars established of the negation of predication can say: 'What is said upon it' means 'what is apt to be predicated upon it', except that their counting of the definition (hadd) with respect to the defined as one of the categories of what is said in answer to 'What is it?', along with their interpretation of 'what is said' as 'the predicate', necessitates that the definition as a definition is a predicate of the defined, which undermines the negation of predication in definition. His statement: 'what is apt to be predicated upon it' means not at the time of definition. The objection by the commentator (al-Muḥannī) against his statement that 'what is apt... etc.' would entail making the definition include countless other things; this is refuted by the fact that those other things are excluded by the condition 'for the purpose of conceptualizing it', and the predication of those other things not in the state of definition only yields assent, not conceptualization. Al-Isam said: Among the things that support the consideration of predication in definition is that the verbal combination of the definer and the definiendum is a complete combination, and it does not fall under any category of non-informative (insha) constructions; thus it must be an informative (khabari) construction containing a judgment.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on the nature of predication (haml) in definitions (ta'rīf). It opens by quoting the matn statement 'What is said upon it (ma yqalu 'alayh) is a genus including the definer and other things.' The commentator then explains that some logicians, like al-Sayyid al-Sharif, hold that predication in definitions is only apparent, not real. For instance, if you say 'Man is a rational animal' (al-insānu hayawānun nāṭiqun), in form 'man' is subject and 'rational animal' is predicate, but in reality no judgment is intended because the purpose is conceptualization (tasawwur), not assent (tasdiq). If it were real predication, it would give assent, contradicting the author's aim. Moreover, in reality, what is judged are the individuals, whereas definitions are of quiddities, so the meaning is like 'the rational animal' with an implied explanatory 'ay' (i.e., 'i.e.'). The passage then presents al-Dawwānī's view, supported by Mīr Zāhid, that the primary purpose of definition is indeed conceptualization of the definiendum, but this conceptualization requires a real predication, though the resulting assent is not the essential aim. The subject has two aspects: individuals (afrād) and concept (mafhūm). In predication, we consider the individuals (the subjects of judgment), but in definition we consider the concept. Confusion between these led some to violate grammatical rules by positing an explanatory 'ay' and denying subject-predicate structure. The commentator refutes the denial of predication, arguing that grammarians universally accept an estimated subject in such constructions. Al-Dawwānī further argues that if one wants to avoid predication in definition, they can interpret 'ma yqalu 'alayh' as 'what is apt to be predicated', but this is undermined by the fact that definitions are counted among the categories of answers to 'what is it?', which are predicates. Finally, al-‘Isām supports predication by noting that the combination of definer and definiendum is a complete informative (khabarī) sentence, not an exclamatory or interrogative one, so it must contain a judgment. Throughout, the text uses examples like 'Zayd is standing' and 'Man is a rational animal', and references the hadith of Jibrīl regarding faith. The overall argument is that real predication occurs in definitions, but the primary cognitive purpose is conceptualization, not assent.

Key Terms
تركيب تام
إنشاء
خبري
تجرّد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-ʿIṣām's argument in the passage, what type of construction is the combination of definer and definiendum?
A) An inshāʾ (non-informative) construction like an exclamation.
B) A complete combination (tarkīb tāmm) that must be khabarī (informative).
C) An incomplete combination that requires an explanatory 'ay'.
D) A defective construction with no subject or predicate.

Key Takeaway
The undeniable grammatical structure of definition sentences forces the conclusion that predication is real, even if its ultimate purpose is conceptualization.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the sentence 'al-ʿilmu ḥuwa al-ʿilm bi al-shayʾ ʿalā mā huwa ʿalayh' (Knowledge is the cognition of something as it is). Apply al-ʿIṣām's argument: is it a tarkīb tāmm? Is it inshāʾ or khabar? Conclude whether it contains a judgment.
?
In a debate, your opponent claims that 'Zakātu mālan maʿlūman' (Zakat is a specified wealth) has no real predication because it is a definition. Using grammatical rules, show that a subject must be estimated and the sentence is khabarī.

The Predication Debate in Definition: Grammatical and Logical Responses
Commentator critiques the denial of haml and presents resolutions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct and evaluate the argument that definition involves predication (haml) despite claims to the contrary.

Core Idea
Definition sentences are declarative; denying predication contradicts both grammar and logic.

Some later logicians argued that in a definition like 'man is a rational animal', there is no actual predication because the definiendum and definiens are not distinct. The commentator refutes this using grammatical rules and al-Dawwani's reinterpretation. This lesson walks through the debate and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Locate where the commentator reports the denial of haml between definiendum and definiens. What is the exact position and who is it attributed to?
2
Examine the grammatical refutation
The commentator argues that grammarians do recognize predication in such sentences. Look for the phrase 'the subject is estimated' and understand why the grammatical argument fails.
3
Analyze al-Dawwani's solution
Al-Dawwani proposes that 'what is said about it' means 'apt to be predicated' not actual predication. How does this try to salvage the denial?
4
Evaluate the objection and response
The commentator raises an objection that this would include too many things. How does he exclude them using the condition of conception (tasawwur)?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خلقية العطار والفهم المستقيمُ .ا.هـ. ونقل المحنِّي عَن السَّيِّدِ إنكار الحمل بين المعرف والمعرَّفِ، وفرَّعَ عليه أنَّا إذا قُلْنَا في جوابِ ما الإنسانُ : حيوان ناطق ؛ لا يقدَّرُ لَهُ مبتدأ ولا خبرٌ، وإِنَّما رُفِعَ؛ لأنَّهُ لَمَّا لم يكن لهُ مَا يعملُ فيهِ؛ أُعطي حركةَ الرَّفْعِ لتجرده، وهو كلام غيرُ مُستَقِيمٍ؛ لأنَّا لا نخرجُ القواعد النحويَّةَ المتكلّفة بإصلاح الألفاظ على الاصطلاحاتِ المنطقيَّةِ ، والنُّحاةُ لا يُنكرونَ الحمل، والمبتدأ عندَهُم مُقدَّرٌ في الصُّورة المذكورة، ولم يستثنهَا أحدٌ من مواضع تقدير المبتدأ أو الخبر لقيام القرينة، فالحُكْمُ عندَهُم مُطَّردٌ، وَمَا ذكرَهُ المحشّي يُوجِبُ تَخصيصاً في کلامِهِم مِنْ عِندِ نفسِهِ، وكأنَّ بعض أشياخِنَا اغتر بمثل هذا الكلام فقالَ: إنَّ مثل قولنا : الإنسان حيوان ناطق ؛ أنَّهُ على حذفِ «أي» التفسيريَّةِ، وتَعليلُ الرَّفْعِ بِمَا ذكَرَ مُخالفٌ لِمَا أجمعُوا عليهِ مِنْ أَنَّ الرَّفعَ بالتَّجرُّدِ مُختصّ بالمضارع؛ مَعَ لزومِ أَنْ يكونَ الأسماء قبلَ التَّركيب كلها مرفوعةً بِمُقتَضَى هذا التعليل، قالَ الدَّوَّاني : ومنْ أراد المحافظة على ما قرَّرَهُ بعضُ المتأخّرينَ مِن انتفاء الحمل ; فَلَهُ أنْ يقول : المرادُ بِمَا يُقالُ عليه ما من شأنه أن يحمل عليهِ؛ إلا أنَّ عدَّهم الحدَّ بالنسبة إلى المحدود؛ من أصناف المقول في جواب ما هو، مع تفسيرهم المقول بالمحمول؛ يوجبُ كونَ الحدّ مِن حيثُ إِنَّهُ حدٌ ; مقولاً وَمَحمولاً على محدودِهِ، وهذا خادش لِمَا قرَّرَهُ بعضُهُمْ مِنَ انتفاء الحمل في التَّعريف .ا.هـ. وقَولُهُ: مَا مِنْ شَأْنِهِ أَنْ يحمل عليهِ; أي: لا في حالِ التَّعريفِ، وَمَا تعقَّبَ بِهِ المحشّي كلامَهُ بأَنَّ قولَهُ: مَا مِنْ شأنه ... إلخ; يلزمُ عليهِ جعلَ التَّعريف شاملاً لأغيارٍ أكثرَ مِن أنْ تُحصَى; مَدفوع بخروج هذه الأغيار بقيد لإفادة تصورِهِ، وأمَّا حمل تلك الأغيار لا في حالِ التَّعريف ; فإنَّما تفيدُ التَّصديق دونَ التَّصورِ،  َقالَ العصامُ: وَمِمَّا يؤيّدُ اعتبار الحمل في التَّعريف; أنَّ تركيب لفظي المعرّفِ والمعرَّف ; تركيب تام، وليس داخلاً في شيء من أقسام الإنشاء، فَلَا بُدَّ أنْ يكونَ تَركيباً خبريًّا مُشتَمِلاً على الحُكْم والحمل، ويؤيد عدم اعتبارِهِ أنَّ الحُكْمَ ليس على الأفراد، إذ التَّعريفُ إِنَّما يكونُ لا للأفراد، وليس على الطبيعة لِعَدَم صِدْقِهِ قطعاً ا.هـ.
A commentary: 'Khulqiyya al-Attar and the sound understanding.' He transmitted from al-Muhanni from al-Sayyid the denial of predication between the definiendum and the definiens, and he branched from that that when we answer 'What is man?' with 'a rational animal', no subject nor predicate is estimated for it, but rather it is raised (in nominative) because when it has nothing to operate on, it is given the movement of raising for its bareness. This statement is unsound because we do not extricate the grammatical rules that are forced to correct expressions from logical conventions; the grammarians do not deny predication, and according to them the subject is estimated in the mentioned form, and no one excluded it from the cases of estimating the subject or predicate due to the presence of a contextual clue. So the rule according to them is consistent, and what the commentator mentioned necessitates a specification of their words from himself. It is as if one of our shaykhs was deceived by such talk and said: 'An expression like 'man is a rational animal' involves the deletion of the explanatory 'ay', and the explanation of the nominative with what was mentioned contradicts what they agreed upon, that the raising by bareness is specific to the present tense verb, along with the necessary consequence that nouns before composition would all be nominative according to this explanation.' Al-Dawwani said: 'Whoever wishes to preserve what some later scholars established of the absence of predication can say: what is meant by 'what is said about it' is that which is apt to be predicated on it, except that their counting of the definition in relation to the definiendum as a type of the answer to 'what is it?', along with their interpretation of 'what is said' as 'what is predicated', necessitates that the definition insofar as it is a definition is said and predicated of its definiendum. This mars what some of them established of the absence of predication in definition.' And his statement: 'what is apt to be predicated on it' means not in the state of definition. And what the commentator refuted his statement with, that his saying 'what is apt...' etc. entails making the definition include more others than can be counted, is repelled by the exclusion of these others by a condition to convey its conception; as for the predication of those others not in the state of definition, it only yields assent without conception. Al-'Isam said: 'Among what supports the consideration of predication in definition is that the verbal composition of the definiens and definiendum is a complete composition, and does not fall under any of the types of non-declarative speech; so it must be a declarative composition containing judgment and predication. And what supports not considering it is that the judgment is not about individuals, since definition is only about not individuals, nor about the nature because it is not true of it at all.'
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) that expands on the debate over whether definition involves predication (haml). The author first reports a claim from al-Muhanni via al-Sayyid denying predication between definiendum and definiens, with the argument that in answering 'What is man?' with 'rational animal', there is no grammatical subject or predicate, only a nominative case due to isolation. The author refutes this, arguing that grammarians do recognize predication here, with an estimated subject. He then quotes al-Dawwani, who tries to salvage the denial by reinterpreting 'what is said about it' as 'apt to be predicated', but notes this contradicts the standard view that definitions are predicated. The author then responds to an objection that this would include too many things, clarifying that the condition 'to convey its conception' excludes them; predication of other things not in definition yields only assent, not conception. Finally, al-'Isam argues that the linguistic structure of definition is declarative, requiring judgment and predication, but notes the counterargument that the judgment is not about individuals or nature.

Key Terms
الحمل
المعرف (المعرف والمعرَّف)
التصور
التصديق

A) Grammarians deny predication altogether.
B) Grammarians rule that an estimated subject exists in such sentences.
C) Definitions are imperative sentences, which have no subject.
D) The predicative structure is only figurative.

Key Takeaway
Definition sentences are declarative; they involve predication, but the predication aims at conception, not assent.
