Tasawwur vs Tasdiq: The Purpose of Predication in Definition
Distinction between tasawwur and tasdiq in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between tasawwur and tasdiq in the context of definition and explain how this distinction resolves the predication debate.

Core Idea
Definition aims at conception, not assent; predication in definition is a means to conceive, not to judge truth.

The debate on predication in definition leads to a deeper question: what is the purpose of definition? Al-Dawwani's solution and the subsequent objection highlight the difference between tasawwur (conception) and tasdiq (assent). This lesson unpacks that distinction and al-'Isam's argument about the declarative structure of definition.

Guided Path
1
Recall the problem
The denial of predication leads to a problem: if definition does not involve predication, how does it convey knowledge? Al-Dawwani's 'apt to be predicated' tries to avoid actual predication.
2
Identify the objection
The commentator objects that al-Dawwani's solution makes definition too broad, including many things that are only 'apt' to be predicated. How does he resolve this?
3
Understand the resolution using tasawwur and tasdiq
The response is that the condition 'to convey its conception' (tafwid tasawwurihi) excludes irrelevant predications. Those other predications yield only tasdiq (assent), not tasawwur (conception). Definition aims at tasawwur.
4
Analyze al-'Isam's argument
Al-'Isam argues that the linguistic form of definition is declarative, containing judgment and predication. But he also notes the counterargument that the judgment in definition is not about individuals or nature. This shows the tension between linguistic form and logical purpose.

The Definiens and Its Purpose: Excluding Non-Conception Predications
Commentator explains the definiens condition and responds to Abu al-Fath's critiques.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the defining condition of a definiens (conveying conception) and explain why predications like those of a doubter do not qualify as definitions.

Core Idea
A definiens must convey conception, not merely serve as a predicate in a judgment.

This passage clarifies the essential function of a definiens: it must produce a conception of the definiendum in the mind. The commentator explains that this criterion excludes predicates that do not aim at conception, such as those in statements by a doubter or sleeper. Abu al-Fath's critique highlights potential counterexamples that test this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key criterion
The commentator states that 'the conveyance of its conception' is the purpose of definition. Identify this condition in the Arabic: 'لإفادة تصوره'.
This criterion distinguishes true definitions from other predications.
2
Understand the exclusion of non-conception predicates
The phrase 'excludes what is other than it' means that any predicate that does not aim to convey the conception of the subject is not a definiens. For example, a statement like 'Zayd is standing' conveys a judgment, not a conception.
This includes declarative sentences that only assert a fact.
3
Analyze Abu al-Fath's first objection
Abu al-Fath argues that a declarative composition (khabar) can convey judgment even without an actual predicate, like the statement of a doubter. This challenges the exclusivity of the definition criterion.
The reply presumably maintains that such utterances do not convey conception of the subject.
4
Analyze his second objection
He further objects that a judgment about the nature (tabi'a) can extend to individuals without explicitly considering them, as in quantified propositions. This relates to the scope of definition.
The commentator implies that the judgment about nature is still a judgment, not a definition.

Source Text

فَصْلٌ: فِي المَعَرْفِ وَأَقْسَامِهِ . وقوله : «الإفادة تصوره» يُخرج ما عداه. الدسوقي العطار. ونظر فيه أبو الفتح، أمَّا أَوَّلاً ; فَلِأَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكونَ الكلام تركيباً خَبريًّا باعتبارِ دلالتِهِ على الحُكْم ; وإِنْ لم يتحقق خبرٌ كَخبرِ الشَّاكُ والنَّائم والسَّاهي على ما تقرَّرَ في موضعِهِ ، وأَمَّا ثانياً ; فَلِأَنَّهُ يجوز أن يكونَ الحُكْمُ على الطَّبيعة على وجه يسري إلى الأفراد وإن لم تلاحظ الأفراد على ما هو التَّحقيق في أحكام المحصوراتِ، على أنا لا نسلّم كذبَ الحكم على الطَّبيعة بطريق الطبيعة أيضاً .ا.هـ. وبقي هَهُنا إشكال نفيس أوردَهُ القطبُ الرَّازِيُّ في رسالتِهِ المعمولة في العلوم المختلفة، وهو المختلفة، وهو أَنَّهُ إذا كانَ الغرضُ مِنَ الحمل في التَّعريفِ التَّصوير ; يشكل عليه قولُ جبريل عليهِ السَّلامُ : صَدَقْتَ ; حينَ أجَابَهُ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لَمَّا سألَ عَنْ حقيقة الإيمانِ ماذا هو ؟ فقالَ الرَّسُولُ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الإيمانُ أنْ تؤْمِنَ بِالله وملائكته وكتبه ورسله واليوم الآخِرِ وتؤمن بالقدرِ خَيْرِهِ وَشَرِّهِ» ; لأنَّ التَّصدِيقَ إِنَّما يكون في القضيَّة، وحاصل الجوابِ أَنَّ التَّعريفَ إِنَّما يستقيم إذا كان المعرَّفُ مُساوياً للمعرّفِ ; أي: يصدقُ كُلُّ منهما على ما صدق عليهِ الآخَرُ ، وبالعكس; فيكونُ لِقَولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم جهتانِ ; جهة التّصوير : وَهِيَ التّعريفُ، وجهة أَنَّ مَا صدق عليه الإيمان يصدق عليه الاعتقاد بالله وملائكته التصديق : وهي ... إلخ، فتصديقُ جبريل راجع إلى جهةِ التَّصديق لا إلى جهة التصوير ا . هـ . (قَوْلُهُ : لِإِفَادَةِ تَصَوُّرِهِ) خرج بهذا القيدِ المحمولُ الَّذي لا يكون الغرضُ منه إفادةَ التَّصورِ، قال المحشّي : والمراد لإفادة المبدأ تصوره; لأنَّ المفيد هو المبدأ، والمعرَّفُ مُعدٌ كَمَا قيلَ أو في حكم المعدّ في عدم وجوبِ اجتماعِهِ مَعَ المعرِّفِ ; لأنَّهُ كَثيراً ما ينتفي مع بقاء المعرف، فنسبة الإفادة إليه مجازا . هـ. أرادَ أَنَّ المفيد المبدأ الفيَّاضُ، وهو العقل العاشرُ ; لأنَّهُ المراد عندَهُم وصرَّحُوا بِهِ، فَتفسيرُ البعض المبدأ بِالشَّخص ; خروجٌ عَنِ اصطلاحِهِم ، مَعَ أَنَّ إِسنادُهَا إِلَيْهِ كَإسنادِهَا هو.
Chapter: On the Definiens and its Divisions. His statement: 'the conveyance of its conception' excludes what is other than it. Al-Dasuqi, al-Attar. Abu al-Fath examined it: firstly, because it is permissible that the speech be a declarative composition by virtue of its indication of judgment even if no actual predicate is realized, like the report of the doubter, the sleeper, and the forgetful as established in its place; secondly, because it is permissible that the judgment be about the nature in a way that extends to individuals even if individuals are not considered, according to the verification in the rules of quantified propositions, and we do not admit the falsity of the judgment about the nature by way of nature itself. There remains here a precious problem raised by Qutb al-Razi in his treatise composed on the various sciences – and it is: if the purpose of predication in definition is picturing (taswir), it would be problematic in light of Jibril's statement 'You have spoken the truth' when the Prophet answered him when he asked about the reality of faith: 'What is it?' The Messenger said: 'Faith is to believe in Allah, His angels, His books, His messengers, the Last Day, and to believe in divine decree, its good and evil' – because tasdiq occurs only in a judgment. The gist of the answer is that the definition is valid only if the definiendum and definiens are coextensive, i.e., each applies to everything the other applies to, and vice versa; thus the Prophet's statement has two aspects: a picturing aspect, which is the definition, and a tasdiq aspect – that what faith applies to, belief in Allah etc. also applies – so Jibril's tasdiq goes back to the tasdiq aspect, not the taswir aspect. (His statement: 'to convey its conception') – this condition excludes the predicate whose purpose is not to convey conception. The commentator said: 'What is meant is the conveyance of its conception by the Active Intellect (al-mabda'), because the conveyor is the Active Intellect, and the definiendum is a preparer (mu'add) as it is said, or in the ruling of a preparer, in that its conjunction with the definiens is not necessary because it often ceases while the definiens remains, so the attribution of conveyance to it is metaphorical.' He meant that the conveyor is the Effusive Intellect (al-mabda' al-fayyad), which is the Tenth Intellect, because that is what they mean and they stated it explicitly; so the interpretation of 'al-mabda'' by some as 'the person' is a departure from their convention, although the attribution of conveyance to it is like the attribution of conveyance to him.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on the definiens and its divisions. The commentator first notes that the phrase 'the conveyance of its conception' excludes other types of predication. Then Abu al-Fath critiques this: first, a declarative sentence may convey judgment even without an actual predicate, like statements from a doubter; second, judgment may be about the nature in a way that covers individuals, as in quantified propositions. Next, a problem from Qutb al-Razi is presented: if the purpose of predication in definition is taswir (picturing/conception), why did Jibril say 'You have spoken the truth' after the Prophet's definition of iman, since tasdiq belongs to judgments? The answer: the definition has two aspects: taswir (the definition itself) and tasdiq (the correspondence of definiendum and definiens). Jibril's tasdiq refers to the correspondence, not to the definitional function. The final part explains that 'conveyance of its conception' is ultimately attributed to the Active Intellect (the Tenth Intellect) as the efficient cause of understanding, the definiendum being only a preparatory factor; any interpretation of 'al-mabda'' as a human person is a deviation from standard terminology.

المعرّف
التصوير
المحمول
المبدأ

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, which of the following would NOT qualify as a definiens?
A) 'Man is a rational animal'
B) 'Zayd is standing' (said by a doubter)
C) 'Faith is belief in Allah, His angels, etc.'
D) 'The triangle is a three-sided polygon'

Key Takeaway
A definiens must convey the conception (taswir) of the definiendum; predicates that merely express judgment do not fulfill the defining function.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a definition of 'salah' from a fiqh manual and determine whether the definiens conveys conception or merely states a judgment. Justify your answer.
?
Construct a definition of 'iman' that meets the criterion of conveying conception, then separate the taswir and tasdiq aspects.
